(It is permissible) i.e., it is valid to confine oneself to water alone, and it is the best after combining water and stone in virtue; or stone, which is inferior to both in virtue. The sunnah is attained even if virtue differs. (The sunnah is cleaning the area) because that is the objective. (The number in making stones three is mandub) due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever uses stones for istinja, let him make it an odd number.' Because it is probable that it indicates permission, so the number is mandub, (not sunnah mu'akkadah) because of what is reported of choice from his statement: 'Whoever uses stones for istinja, let him make it an odd number; whoever does well, then good; and whoever does not, there is no harm.' For it is definitive in indicating choice. (So he performs istinja), desiring virtue, (with three stones), i.e., completing their number as three, (as mandub if cleaning is achieved) i.e., purification without it. And since the objective is purification, he mentioned a method by which it is achieved in the most complete manner, so he said: (And the method of istinja) with stones is that he wipes with the first stone, beginning from the front, i.e., the penis, to the back; and with the second from the back to the front, which is called idbar; or with the third from front to back. This order is when the testicles are pendulous, whether summer or winter, for fear of soiling them. ... [continues]
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the text of Maraqi al-Falah on the rulings of istinja with stones. It begins by stating that it is permissible to use only water, or only stones, but using both is superior. The sunnah of istinja is to clean the area (inqa' al-mahal), not necessarily the number of stones. Using three stones is mandub (recommended), not sunnah mu'akkadah, based on the Prophet's hadith 'Whoever uses stones, let him make it an odd number.' The hadith is interpreted as permissive (ibaha) rather than obligatory, because another version includes 'whoever does, good; whoever does not, no harm.' The author then details the method: for a man with pendulous testicles, he should wipe from front to back first, then back to front, then front to back. If testicles are not pendulous, he begins from back to front for better cleaning. Women start from front to back to avoid soiling the vulva. After wiping, he washes his hand with water, then rubs the area with water using one or two fingers (or three if needed). The commentary notes that the exact method is not rigid; the goal is purification. It also warns against using only one finger (causes disease) and against inserting finger into anus (causes piles). For women, they should use the little and middle fingers together to avoid pleasure. Various authorities are cited: Ibn Amir Haj, al-Sarakhsi, al-Zahidi, al-Qahastani, etc. The relied-upon position is flexibility: one should do what achieves cleanliness without excess.

Key Terms
إقبال (iqbal): Wiping from front to back.
إدبار (idbar): Wiping from back to front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a woman performing istinja with stones, the recommended direction of wiping for each stone is:
A) Front to back for the first stone, back to front for the second, front to back for the third.
B) Back to front for all stones.
C) Front to back for all stones.
D) Any direction as long as the number is odd.

Key Takeaway
The method of istinja is flexible; focus on thorough cleaning and avoid rigid insistence on a fixed sequence.

Method of Istinja: Direction and Finger Technique
Detailed method of istinja with gender-specific instructions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended method of istinja for men and women according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the starting direction.

Core Idea
Begin istinja from back to front for men, front to back for women; use multiple fingers to ensure thorough cleaning and avoid disease.

Proper purification after relieving oneself is essential not only for ritual cleanliness but also for physical health. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on how to perform istinja, including the direction of wiping and which fingers to use. This lesson unpacks the rulings from al-Tahtawi's super-commentary, clarifying the sunnah method and an important difference of opinion among the early Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall hukm of the method
The described technique (direction, finger sequence) is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah). The basic act of istinja (removing impurity) is wajib, but the specific method is recommended for thoroughness and health.
Do not confuse the wajib of removing filth with the sunnah of the method.
2
Determine the direction for men and women
Men: start from back (dubur) to front (qabul). Women: start from front to back to avoid contaminating the vagina.
The direction differs to prevent cross-contamination and facilitate thorough cleaning.
3
Explain the finger technique for men
Raise the middle finger first, then ring, little, and index as needed. Use one, two, or three fingers depending on necessity. Do not use only one finger, as that causes disease and insufficient cleaning.
The middle finger is raised slightly at the start to allow impure water to flow without spreading.
4
Explain the finger technique for women
Women raise the little finger and middle finger together initially to avoid experiencing pleasure from a single finger. The palm may be used for virgins to protect the hymen.
This precaution is unique to the Hanafi school.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on starting direction
Abu Hanifa said to start with the back because it is more important (the source of impurity). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said to start with the front because it is more immediate. The fatwa is upon Abu Hanifa's view.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf with a clear mufta bihi.

And if it is not hanging/suspended, he begins from back to front because it is more thorough in cleaning. And the woman begins from front to back fearing contamination of her private part. Commentary
This passage is a hashiah (super-commentary) on Maraqi al-Falah, detailing the method of istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself). It provides specific rulings on the direction of wiping for men and women, the sequence of fingers, and the number of fingers to use. For men, the preferred direction is from back to front to maximize cleaning; for women, from front to back to avoid contaminating the vagina. The commentary emphasizes using multiple fingers, raising the middle finger first to facilitate flow, then others as needed. Using only one finger is discouraged for health reasons. For women, using little and middle fingers together is recommended to avoid pleasure. The discussion also covers washing hands, rubbing with water, and the prohibition of inserting the finger into the anus. A supplementary note (tatimma) addresses a dispute: Abu Hanifa says to start with the back (dubur), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say start with the front (qabul); the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view. The commentary synthesizes multiple Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
استنجاء (istinja): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself, typically with water or stones.
مدلاة (mudallah): A hanging object; 'ghayr mudallah' means not using a suspended object, referring to direct water use.

The Ruling on Mubalaghah in Istinja
Clarifying the ruling on mubalaghah in istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that mubalaghah is sunnah and explain why no fixed number is prescribed.

Core Idea
Istinja cleanliness is achieved by certainty, not by counting.

A common question in purification is whether a specific number of washes is required. The Hanafi school, as explained by al-Tahtawi, holds that no number is fixed; rather, the person cleans until certainty or predominant conjecture of purity is reached. For those plagued by obsessive doubts, some limits have been suggested, but the correct view is that these limits are not for the general person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under discussion is mubalaghah (exerting thorough cleaning) in istinja.
2
Recognize no fixed number
The passage states that no specific number of washes is prescribed; the correct view delegates the amount to personal judgment.
3
Understand the reasoning
The goal is to achieve certainty or predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) of purity, not to fulfill a ritual count.
4
Note the exception for waswasi
For a person prone to obsessive doubts (waswasi), some scholars proposed fixed numbers (e.g., three, seven) to prevent excess, but the correct view is that the delegation to opinion applies to non-waswasi individuals.
The commentator clarifies that the view suggesting limits is not the correct one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويبالغ المستنجي في التنظيف حتى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة) ولم يقدر بعدد لأن الصحيح تفويضه إلى الرأي حتى يطمئن القلب بالطهارة بيقين أو غلبة الظن، وقيل يقدر في حق الموسوس بسبع، أو ثلاث وقيل في الإحليل بثلاث وفي المقعدة بخمس، وقيل بتسع، وقيل بعشر (و) يبالغ في إرخاء المقعدة) ليزيل ما في الشرج بقدر الإمكان إن لم یکن صائماً) والصائم لا يبالغ حفظاً الفساد ويحترز أيضاً. للصوم عن من إدخال الأصبع مبتلة لأنه يفسد الصوم فإذا فرغ من الاستنجاء بالماء غسل يده ثانيا ونشف مقعدته قبل القيام) لئلا تجذب المقعدة شيئاً من الماء إذا كان (صائماً ويستحب لغير الصائم حفظ الثوب عن الماء المستعمل . قوله : (حتى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة) أي عن المحل وعن اصبعه التي استنجى بها لأن الرائحة أثر النجاسة فلا طهارة مع بقائها إلا أن يشق والناس عنه غافلون قالوا: ويبالغ في الاستنجاء في الشتاء فوق ما يبالغ في الصيف لصلابة المحل في الشتاء إلا أن يستنجي بماء حار لأنه يرخي المحل ويشرع بالإزالة فلا يحتاج إلى شدة المبالغة لكن لا يبلغ ثواب المستنجي بماء بارد لأنه أفضل وأنفع كما في الفتاوي وغيره وأفضليته لمشقته وأنفعيته لقطع الباسور. قوله : (وقيل يقدر في حق الموسوس) بفتح الواو جعله المصنف مقابلاً للصحيح والذي ذكره غيره أن الصحيح محله في غير الموسوس فهو من القائل به لا مقابله أفاده السيد وغيره قوله : (بقدر الإمكان) متعلق بقوله يبالغ . قوله : (حفظاً للصوم عن الفساد) في الخلاصة من كتاب الصوم إنما يفسد إذا وصل الماء إلى موضع الحقنة وقلما يكون ذلك اهـ وفي القهستاني من كتاب الصوم ومع هذا في إفساد الصوم بذلك خلاف اهـ وما قيل إنه لا يتنفس شديداً حفظاً للصوم فحرج ولا فائدة فيه فإنه لا يصل بالتنفس شيء إلى الداخل أصلاً أفاده العلامة نوح وفي السراج وغيره إذا خرج دبره وهو صائم فغسله لا يقوم حتى ينشفه قبل رده فإن رجع قبل التنشيف مبتلاً أفطر اهـ. قوله: (ونشف مقعدته بخرقة، أو بيده اليسرى مرة بعد أخرى إن لم تكن خرقة. استثناء
He said: (And the one performing istinja should exert thoroughly in cleaning until he removes the bad smell) And no number was specified because the correct view is to delegate it to opinion until the heart is assured of purity with certainty or predominant conjecture. And it is said that it is measured for the obsessively scrupulous person by seven, or three; and it is said for the urethra by three and for the anus by five, and it is said by nine, and it is said by ten. (And) he should exert in relaxing the anus to remove what is in the rectum as much as possible if he is not fasting. And the fasting person should not exert to preserve the fast from corruption, and he should also guard against inserting a wet finger because it breaks the fast. So when he finishes istinja with water, he washes his hand a second time and dries his anus before standing, lest the anus draw some water if he is fasting. And it is recommended for the non-fasting person to protect his garment from used water.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This section of the hashiah comments on the matn phrase 'and he should exert thoroughly in cleaning until he removes the bad smell.' It explains that no fixed number of washes is required; rather, the correct view is to rely on one's judgment until certainty or predominant conjecture of cleanliness is reached. For those prone to waswas (obsessive doubts), some scholars recommend limits like seven or three for the urethra. The text then discusses exerting by relaxing the anus to ensure removal of impurities, but for a fasting person, such exertion is avoided to prevent water entering internally and breaking the fast. Similarly, inserting a wet finger is prohibited for the fasting person. After completing istinja, the fasting person should wash his hand again and dry his anus before standing to avoid drawing water inside. For non-fasting individuals, it is recommended to protect the garment from used water. The commentary also notes that using cold water for istinja is more virtuous and beneficial, especially for preventing piles, although hot water may be easier. The discussion on the waswasi person clarifies that the opinion setting limits is not the correct view; rather, the correct view is for non-waswasi individuals. There is also a detailed analysis of what breaks the fast, with references to al-Khulasa and al-Qahistani, concluding that water reaching the injection site (mahall al-huqnah) would break the fast, but that is rare.

Key Terms
مبالغة (mubalaghah): Exerting extra effort in cleaning to ensure removal of impurity and odor.
موسوس (waswasi): A person prone to obsessive doubts in purification; special rulings apply to them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct Hanafi view on the number of washes in istinja?
A) Three washes are obligatory
B) Seven washes are recommended
C) No fixed number; it is delegated to personal opinion
D) One wash is sufficient if the impurity is removed

Key Takeaway
Mubalaghah in istinja is sunnah; the number of washes is left to the individual's discretion until certainty or predominant conjecture.

Precautions for a Fasting Person During Istinja
Rules for istinja while fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the actions a fasting person must avoid during istinja and the steps to preserve the fast.

Core Idea
A fasting person must prevent water from entering the body during cleaning.

The hashiah continues with special rules for a fasting person. While mubalaghah is recommended for others, a fasting person should avoid excessive exertion to prevent water from entering the rectum. Additionally, inserting a wet finger is prohibited. After finishing istinja, the fasting person must wash hands again and dry the anus before standing to avoid drawing water inside. These rules ensure the validity of the fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special status
The ruling applies specifically to a person who is fasting.
2
Avoid mubalaghah
The fasting person should not exert thoroughly (mubalaghah) in cleaning, as this may cause water to enter the body and break the fast.
3
Avoid wet finger insertion
Inserting a wet finger during istinja is prohibited for the fasting person because it can introduce water and invalidate the fast.
4
After washing, dry before standing
The fasting person must wash his hand again after istinja and dry his anus before standing up to prevent residual water from being drawn inside.
The passage emphasizes this step to avoid breaking the fast.
5
Understand the rationale
All these precautions aim to avoid any water entering the body, which would nullify the fast. The commentary notes that actual breaking occurs only if water reaches the internal injection site, but caution is required.

Source Text

Virgin's Method of Istinja
Ruling on virgin's istinja method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a virgin's istinja and explain the reason for using the palm rather than fingers.

Core Idea
To protect the hymen, a virgin performs istinja with her palm, not fingers.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling in taharah for women: how a virgin should perform istinja after using the toilet. The general method of istinja involves using the left hand and water, but for a virgin, the fingers could risk damaging the hymen. Therefore, the school prescribes using the palm of the hand. We will examine the ruling, the reason, and a difference of opinion among scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the subject
The act is istinja (cleansing after using the toilet) for a virgin woman. Determine why she is treated differently from other women.
The term 'virgin' here refers to a woman with an intact hymen.
2
State the primary ruling
The matn states that a virgin should not use her fingers but the palm of her hand. This is the correct view.
The source of this ruling is the fear of removing (damaging) the hymen.
3
Identify the reason (illah)
The reason is 'خوفاً من إزالة العذرة' – out of fear of removing the hymen. The illah is the protection of the hymen.
If the hymen is already broken (non-virgin), this ruling does not apply.
4
Note the variant opinion
Some scholars, including Ibn Amir Hajj, claim that using fingertips is acceptable because the hymen is only at risk from internal insertion, not external rubbing. They argue that proper cleaning requires fingertips.
This opinion is not mufta bihi; the relied-upon view is the first.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) is that the virgin uses the palm of her hand. This is confirmed in al-Hindiyya and al-Siraj as the chosen and correct view.
The hashiah leaves the reader with the first view as the reliable position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعذراء لا تستنجي بأصابعها بل براحة كفها خوفاً من إزالة العذرة يكفيها أن تغسل براحتها هو الصحيح وفي الهندية هو المختار وفي السراج هو قول العامة وقيل تستنجي برؤس أصابعها لأنها تحتاج إلى تطهير فرجها الخارج ولا يحصل ذلك إلا برؤس الأصابع ورجحه ابن أمير حاج قال والإستماع موهوم لأنه فيما يظهر إنما يكون بالإدخال في الفرج الداخل.
And the virgin does not perform istinja with her fingers but with the palm of her hand, out of fear of removing the hymen. It suffices her to wash with her palm; that is the correct view. In al-Hindiyya it is the chosen view, and in al-Siraj it is the view of the general scholars. And it was said: she performs istinja with her fingertips because she needs to clean her external private part, and that is only achieved with fingertips, and Ibn Amir Hajj favored this, saying: 'And the hearing is baseless, because it only occurs by insertion into the internal private part.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on istinja for a virgin woman. The matn states that she should not use her fingers but rather the palm of her hand, to avoid damaging the hymen (عذرة). The hashiah explains that the correct position in the school is that washing with the palm is sufficient, as stated in al-Hindiyya and al-Siraj. However, there is a minority opinion that she should use her fingertips to ensure thorough cleaning of the external area. Ibn Amir Hajj preferred this second view, arguing that the fear of hymen removal only applies to internal insertion, not external rubbing. The hashiah does not explicitly resolve this ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi is the first position (palm). The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the variant opinions.

Key Terms
العذرة (al-'udhrah): The hymen, a membrane in the virgin's private part.
بَرَاحَةِ الْكَفِّ (barāhati al-kaff): The palm of the hand, not the fingers.

No Fixed Number for Istinja: Reliance on Judgment
Ruling on the extent of cleansing after relieving oneself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of wipes in istinja and identify the exceptions for the waswasi (obsessive) person.

Core Idea
Istinja has no fixed number of wipes; cleanliness is determined by one's own judgment until certainty or dominant probability.

In this lesson, we examine a classic ruling from the Hanafi school about how many times one should wipe after relieving oneself. The base text states there is no fixed number, while the commentary expands on the concession for those suffering from obsessive doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Read the matn: it explicitly states no fixed number (لم يقدر بعدد) and delegates the decision to personal judgment (تفويضه إلى الرأي).
This is the default rule for all individuals.
2
Understand the Criterion
The standard is to clean until the foul smell is removed, based on certainty (يقين) or dominant probability (غلبة الظن).
Absolute certainty is not required; sufficient confidence is enough.
3
Note the Exception for the Waswasi
For a person with obsessive doubts (الموسوس), some opinions fix a number (3,5,7,9,10) to limit their anxiety. The hashiah clarifies that these numbers are a concession, not the general rule.
The fixed numbers apply only to the waswasi; others follow the general rule.
4
Distinguish the Correct View
The hashiah states that the 'correct' (صحيح) view applies to non-waswasi; the fixed numbers are from those who say it (من القائل به), not its opposite.
Do not mistakenly apply fixed numbers to everyone.
5
Apply Seasonal and Water Nuances
In winter, more effort is needed due to hardness of the area; hot water softens the area and reduces the need. Cold water is more virtuous and beneficial for health.
These details show the school’s attention to practical circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبالغ المستنجي في التنظيف حتى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة ولم يقدر بعدد لأن الصحيح تفويضه إلى الرأي حتى يطمئن القلب بالطهارة بيقين أو غلبة الظن، وقيل يقدر في حق الموسوس بسبع، أو ثلاث وقيل في الإحليل بثلاث وفي المقعدة بخمس، وقيل بتسع، وقيل بعشر. قوله : (حتى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة) أي عن المحل وعن اصبعه التي استنجى بها لأن الرائحة أثر النجاسة فلا طهارة مع بقائها إلا أن يشق والناس عنه غافلون قالوا: ويبالغ في الاستنجاء في الشتاء فوق ما يبالغ في الصيف لصلابة المحل في الشتاء إلا أن يستنجي بماء حار لأنه يرخي المحل ويشرع بالإزالة فلا يحتاج إلى شدة المبالغة لكن لا يبلغ ثواب المستنجي بماء بارد لأنه أفضل وأنفع كما في الفتاوي وغيره وأفضليته لمشقته وأنفعيته لقطع الباسور. قوله : (وقيل يقدر في حق الموسوس) بفتح الواو جعله المصنف مقابلاً للصحيح والذي ذكره غيره أن الصحيح محله في غير الموسوس فهو من القائل به لا مقابله أفاده السيد وغيره.
And the one performing istinja should exert effort in cleansing until he removes the foul smell, and it was not fixed by number because the correct view is to delegate it to opinion until the heart is at ease with purification by certainty or dominant probability. And it was said: it is fixed for the waswasi (obsessive) as seven, or three; and it was said: for the urethra three and for the anus five; and it was said: nine; and it was said: ten. His saying: 'until he removes the foul smell' i.e. from the place and from his finger with which he performed istinja, because the smell is a trace of impurity, so there is no purification with its remaining unless it is difficult, and people are heedless of it. They said: And he should exert more effort in istinja in winter than in summer due to the hardness of the place, unless he uses hot water because it softens the place and begins removal, so he does not need intense exertion, but he does not attain the reward of one who uses cold water because it is better and more beneficial as in al-Fatawa and others, its superiority due to its difficulty and its benefit for cutting hemorrhoids. His saying: 'And it was said: it is fixed for the waswasi' with fatha on the waw, the author made it opposite to the correct, and others mentioned that the correct applies to the non-waswasi, so it is from the one who says it, not its opposite, as stated by al-Sayyid and others.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the extent of cleansing after relieving oneself. The matn states that there is no fixed number of wipes; rather, the person should clean until the odor is gone, relying on personal judgment (ra'y) until certainty or dominant probability is reached. The hashiah explains that the odor is a sign of impurity, so it must be removed unless doing so is excessively difficult. It also mentions that more effort is required in winter due to hardness of the area, but hot water reduces the need because it softens. Cold water is considered more virtuous and beneficial, e.g., for hemorrhoids. Regarding the waswasi (person with obsessive doubts), there are opinions limiting the number to three, five, seven, nine, or ten, but the hashiah clarifies that the 'correct' position refers to non-waswasi individuals; the fixed numbers are only for the waswasi as a concession, not the general rule. The author follows the order: first the general ruling, then the exception for the obsessive.

Key Terms
الموسوس (al-muswas): A person who has obsessive doubts (waswasa) about purity.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-dhann): Dominant probability, a level of certainty sufficient for legal rulings when absolute certainty is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Order of Washing in Istinja: Front or Back?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istinja order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the order of washing in istinja, explain the evidence of the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
In istinja, wash the back first – the fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's view for practical reasons.

This brief supplement from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a subtle point: when performing istinja, which area should be washed first – the front (urethra) or the back (anus)? While it may seem trivial, the order reflects a deeper legal reasoning about impurity and practicality. We will explore the internal Hanafi disagreement and learn which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the passage discusses the preferred sequence (tartib) in istinja. The core question: should one start with the front (al-qubul) or the back (al-dubur)?
This is a sunnah, not a fard, so the order does not affect validity.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that one should begin with the back because it is more important (the impurity is more concentrated) and because rubbing the back area may cause residual urine to drip, making prior washing of the front futile.
His proof is practical observation (mushahada) and consideration of maslaha.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) argue that the front should be washed first because it is encountered earlier in the process of wiping.
Their proof is based on the natural order of contact.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'والفتوى على الأول' – the fatwa is on the first view, i.e., Abu Hanifa's. Later Hanafi scholars preferred this due to its practical benefit.
This is an example of tarjih within the madhhab.
5
Understand the practical consequence
In practice, a Hanafi should start with the back. However, if someone accidentally reverses the order, his purification is still valid because the sequence is sunnah, not wajib.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the two views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: اختلف في القبل والدبر بأيهما يبدأ فقال الإمام الأعظم رضي الله تعالى عنه : يبدأ بالدبر لأنه أهم ولأنه بواسطة الدلك في الدبر وما حوله يقطر البول كما هو مشاهد فلا فائدة في تقديم القبل وعندهما بالقبل لأنه أسبق والفتوى على الأول.
Supplement: There is a difference of opinion regarding the front and back, which one to start with. Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa) – may Allah be pleased with him – said: he begins with the back because it is more important, and because by rubbing the back and its surroundings, urine drips as is observed, so there is no benefit in starting with the front. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he begins with the front because it is earlier. And the fatwa is on the first.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the order of washing during istinja. The author presents a supplement (tattimah) to the main text. Abu Hanifa holds that one should start with the back (anus) because it is more important (the impurity is more concentrated) and because rubbing the back area causes urine to drip, so starting with the front would be futile. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the front (urethra) should be washed first because it is encountered earlier in the process. The hashiah records that the fatwa (operative ruling) is on Abu Hanifa's view. The commentary explains the reasoning: priority of importance and practical utility. This is a clear example of a madhhab internal ikhtilaf resolved by tarjih.

Key Terms
تتمة (tatimmah): A supplement or additional note to the main text.
القبل (al-qubul): The front, i.e., the urethral opening or private part in front.
الدبر (al-dubur): The back, i.e., the anus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The front (urethra).
B) The back (anus).
C) Neither; order is irrelevant.
D) Depends on gender.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the preferred order in istinja is to start with the back (anus) – a sunnah based on practical reasoning.

Istinja for a Fasting Person
Ruling on moderate cleaning to avoid breaking fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for istinja for a fasting person according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling when the anus protrudes.

Core Idea
A fasting person must dry the anus before standing to prevent water from breaking the fast.

This lesson explores the fiqh of istinja for a fasting person, focusing on the conditions that preserve the validity of the fast. The source text from Al-Tahtawi's hashiah expands on the base ruling, clarifying when water actually breaks the fast and providing practical steps. Understanding these nuances helps avoid unnecessary nullification of the fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that istinja during fasting has special conditions: the fasting person should not exert excessively in washing to avoid water entering the cavity.
2
Locate the drying requirement
The text explicitly states that the fasting person must dry the anus before standing up (and before retracting if it protrudes) to prevent water absorption.
Drying is done with a cloth or left hand.
3
Analyse the prohibition of excessive washing
The hashiah clarifies that the fast only breaks if water reaches the internal cavity (like an enema area), which is rare. Hence, moderate washing is safe, but excessive is discouraged (makruh).
4
Note the disagreement
The hashiah cites al-Qahistani: there is a difference of opinion on whether water reaching the enema area breaks the fast. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a fasting person's anus protrudes during istinja, he must dry it before retracting; otherwise the fast breaks. This is a concrete application from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصائم لا يبالغ حفظاً للصوم عن الفساد. فإذا فرغ من الاستنجاء بالماء غسل يده ثانيا ونشف مقعدته قبل القيام لئلا تجذب المقعدة شيئاً من الماء إذا كان صائماً ويستحب لغير الصائم حفظ الثوب عن الماء المستعمل. قوله : (حفظاً للصوم عن الفساد) في الخلاصة من كتاب الصوم إنما يفسد إذا وصل الماء إلى موضع الحقنة وقلما يكون ذلك اهـ وفي القهستاني من كتاب الصوم ومع هذا في إفساد الصوم بذلك خلاف اهـ وما قيل إنه لا يتنفس شديداً حفظاً للصوم فحرج ولا فائدة فيه فإنه لا يصل بالتنفس شيء إلى الداخل أصلاً أفاده العلامة نوح. وفي السراج وغيره إذا خرج دبره وهو صائم فغسله لا يقوم حتى ينشفه قبل رده فإن رجع قبل التنشيف مبتلاً أفطر اهـ. قوله: (ونشف مقعدته بخرقة، أو بيده اليسرى مرة بعد أخرى إن لم تكن خرقة.
And the fasting person should not exert effort (in washing) to preserve the fast from corruption. When he finishes istinja with water, he washes his hand a second time and dries his anus before standing up, lest the anus absorb some water if he is fasting. And for the non-fasting person, it is recommended to protect the garment from used water. His saying: 'to preserve the fast from corruption' – in al-Khulasa from the book of fasting: it only breaks if water reaches the place of an enema, and that rarely happens. In al-Qahistani from the book of fasting: even so, there is disagreement on breaking the fast by that. And what was said that he should not breathe deeply to preserve the fast is hard and has no benefit, because nothing reaches the inside by breathing at all, as stated by Allamah Nuh. In al-Siraj and others: if his anus protrudes while he is fasting and he washes it, he should not stand until he dries it before retracting it; if he returns it wet before drying, he breaks his fast. His saying: 'and dries his anus with a cloth or with his left hand repeatedly if there is no cloth.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on istinja for a fasting person. The matn states that the fasting person should not exert excessive effort in washing, to avoid breaking the fast. The hashiah clarifies that the fast is only broken if water reaches the internal cavity (like an enema), which is rare. It also provides an additional ruling: if the anus protrudes during istinja, one must dry it before retracting, otherwise water may be drawn inside and break the fast. The passage then gives a practical instruction: wash hands again and dry the area. This lesson covers the conditions for valid fasting during taharah. The commentary follows the author's order: first the fasting person's restriction, then the drying method.

Key Terms
الحقنة (al-huqnah): Enema, a medical injection into the rectum; water reaching that area breaks the fast.
نشف (nashf): Drying, especially the anus after istinja to prevent water absorption.
لا يبالغ (la yubaligh): Do not exert excessively, i.e., avoid excessive washing that may force water into the body.

Key Takeaway

The Excused Amount of Impurity in Prayer
Ruling on excused amount of impurity beyond the exit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the amount of impurity that invalidates prayer, identify the measure of a dirham for solid and liquid impurities, and apply the exception when removal would require uncovering the 'awrah.

Core Idea
Impurity exceeding a dirham in weight or area invalidates prayer — unless removal would force uncovering the 'awrah.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every impurity invalidates prayer. There is an excused amount known as qadr al-dirham. This lesson explains the threshold, how it is measured, and the important exception when the impurity cannot be removed without exposing the private parts. Understanding this ruling helps you distinguish between valid and invalid prayers in cases of impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and concern
The act is praying while carrying impurity from an exit (e.g., urine). The ruling depends on the amount and location of the impurity.
The impurity must have exited the body; internal impurity is not considered.
2
Determine the threshold
If the impurity exceeds the exit and its amount (the exceeding part alone) is more than a dirham in weight for solids or area for liquids, prayer is invalid.
Dirham weight ~3g; dirham area ~2.5 cm² (palm area).
3
Apply the exclusion rule
Impurity that remains inside the exit is legally disregarded (sāqiṭ al-i'tibār). Only the part that has exited and spread is counted towards the threshold.
If the impurity does not exceed the dirham when counting only the external part, prayer is valid even if some remains inside.
4
Check the removal condition
If the impurity can be removed without uncovering the 'awrah, it must be removed. If removal would require exposing the private parts, then the impurity is excused and prayer is valid with it.
This is based on the principle of avoiding harm and preserving dignity.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a dispute among Hanafis whether the disregard of impurity in the exit is by consensus or not. The relied-upon view is that it is disregarded, and this is not contested in practice.
Knowing the disagreement helps in understanding the strength of the evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تجاوزت النجاسة مخرجها، وزاد المتجاوز بانفراده على قدر الدرهم وزنا في المتجسدة ومساحة في المائعة لا تصح معه الصلاة الزيادته على القدر المعفو عنه إذا وجد ما يزيله من مائع أو ماء ويحتال لإزالته من غير كشف العورة عند من يراه تحرزاً عن إرتكاب المحرم بالقدر الممكن، وأما إذا لم يزد إلا بالضم لما في المخرج فلا يضر تركه لأنّ ما في المخرج ساقط الإعتبار. قوله: (إذا وجد ما يزيله والأصلي معها ولا إعادة كما في الهداية قوله: ( ويحتال الخ) : أي إن أمكنه، وإلا فلا لأن كشف العورة حرام يعذر به في ترك طهارة النجاسة إذا لم يمكنه إزالتها من غير كشف قاله البرهان الحلبي : قوله عند من يراه المراد به من يحرم عليه جماعة ولو أمته المجوسية، والتي زوجها للغير لأنه لما حرم عليه وطؤهما حرم عليه نظرة إلى عورتهما، وكذا نظرهما إليه إذ متى حرم الوطء حرمت الدواعي إلا ما استثني كأمر أنَّه الحائض والنفساء وتمامه في حاشية الدر. قوله : لأنّ ما في المخرج ساقط الاعتبار) : أي على المعتمد خلافاً لمن حكى عليه الإتفاق .
And if the impurity exceeds its exit, and the exceeding part alone is more than a dirham in weight for solid impurity and in area for liquid impurity, prayer is not valid with it. (This is) the excess over the excused amount, when he finds something to remove it, liquid or water, and he should contrive to remove it without uncovering the private part if possible, to avoid committing the prohibited to the extent possible. And if it does not exceed except by adding what is in the exit, then leaving it does not harm, because what is in the exit is disregarded. His saying: 'when he finds something to remove it' – the original (impurity) and it together with no repetition as in al-Hidayah. His saying: 'and he should contrive' i.e. if he can; otherwise, no, because uncovering the private part is prohibited and is an excuse for leaving the purification of impurity if he cannot remove it without uncovering, as stated by Burhan al-Halabi. His saying: 'from the one who sees it' – meaning one who is forbidden to him in marriage, even if his slave woman is a Magian, or one who is married to another, because when intercourse is forbidden, looking at her private parts is also forbidden, and likewise her looking at him, because whenever intercourse is forbidden, its means are forbidden except what is exempted like the case of a menstruating woman and one with postpartum bleeding, and its completion is in Hashiyat al-Durr. His saying: 'because what is in the exit is disregarded' i.e. according to the relied-upon view, contrary to one who claimed consensus on it.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the quantity of impurity that is excused in prayer. It states that if impurity (e.g., urine) spreads beyond the natural exit and exceeds a dirham in weight (for solid) or area (for liquid), prayer is invalid. The hashiah explains the conditions: the excess is measured alone, not including what remains inside the exit, which is legally disregarded. The ruling applies only if one can find something to remove it; if removal would require uncovering the 'awrah, the obligation to remove it is waived because covering is prioritised. The hashiah also clarifies that the exception applies to those with whom one has a mahram relationship or is prohibited to marry. The commentator, Burhan al-Halabi, notes that if removal is impossible without uncovering, the impurity is excused. The authority weight is from al-Hidayah (Zahir al-Riwayah). The final note deals with a disagreement on whether the impurity in the exit is disregarded by consensus or not.

Key Terms
قدر الدرهم (qadr al-dirham): The weight or area of a dirham coin; used as measure for excused impurity.
ساقط الإعتبار (sāqiṭ al-i'tibār): Legally disregarded; not taken into consideration in the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What amount of impurity beyond the exit invalidates prayer according to this passage?
A) Any amount.
B) More than a dirham in weight for solid, area for liquid.
C) More than two dirhams.
D) Only if it covers the whole body.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school excuses impurity in prayer up to the size of a dirham, but only the portion outside the exit is counted, and removal is not required if it would expose the 'awrah.

The Dislike of Using Bone and Dung for Istinja
Ruling on prohibition of bone and dung for istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using bone and dung for istinja and explain the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Bones and dung are makruh for istinja because they are food for the jinn.

This lesson examines a well-known ruling in taharah: the prohibition of using bone or dung for istinja. The Hanafi school classifies this as makruh, based on the Prophet's explicit command. Understanding the evidence and the precise level of dislike is crucial for proper purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is istinja using bone or dung. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text says 'يكره' (it is disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet said: 'Do not perform istinja with dung or bones, for they are food for your brothers among the jinn.'
The hadith is found in Sahih Muslim and other collections.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition (nahy) in the hadith indicates karahah (dislike) in Hanafi usul, not necessarily haram, based on the reason given.
The reason (they are food for jinn) provides a qarina that softens the prohibition.
4
Check for ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Hanbali) consider it haram. The Hanafi school maintains karahah due to the permissibility context.
The disagreement stems from interpreting the nahy.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that it is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
Later Hanafi scholars uphold this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره الاستنجاء بعظم المعتمد وروث لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا تستنجوا بالروث ولا بالعظام فإنهما فرع في الخانية مريض عجز عن الاستنجاء ولم يكن له من يحل له جماعه سقط عنه الإستنجاء لأنه لا يحل فرجه إلا لذلك والله أعلم اهـ.
And it is disliked (makruh) to perform istinja with a bone, according to the reliable view, and with dung, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Do not perform istinja with dung nor with bones, for they are...' Branch: In al-Khaniyya: A sick person who is unable to perform istinja and has no one who is permissible for him to have intercourse, his istinja is dropped because his private part is not permissible except for that. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on what is disliked for istinja. The matn states that using a bone (according to the reliable view) and dung is makruh, based on the hadith that the Prophet forbade using these items because they are food for the jinn. The hashiah adds a brief peripheral ruling (far') from al-Khaniyya: if a sick person cannot perform istinja himself and has no one who is permissible to see his private part (e.g., spouse), the obligation of istinja is dropped. This is a separate ruling but included here as a branch. The commentary focuses on the main ruling: the evidence for the dislike is the hadith. The hashiya clarifies the authority for the bone ruling saying 'المعتمد' (reliable view).

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; here it is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
عظم (azm): Bone; a solid part of an animal skeleton.
روث (rawth): Dung; animal excrement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Recommended (sunnah).
D) Obligatory (wajib).

Key Takeaway
Using bone or dung for istinja is makruh in the Hanafi school due to the Prophet's prohibition, as they are food for the jinn.

Istinja for a Sick Person Unable to Perform It
Branch ruling from al-Khaniyya on sick person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling that the obligation of istinja drops for a sick person who cannot clean himself and has no permissible helper.

Core Idea
If a sick person cannot perform istinja and has no spouse or mahram to help, the obligation is dropped.

This lesson covers a specific case from al-Khaniyya: a sick person who cannot perform istinja and has no one permissible (halal) to see his private part for cleaning. The ruling is that istinja is no longer required. This illustrates the principle of necessity (darurah) in taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and condition
The actor is a sick person unable to perform istinja himself.
The text says 'مريض عجز عن الاستنجاء' (a sick person unable to perform istinja).
2
Assess the available helper
There is no one permissible (halal) to see his private part, meaning no spouse or mahram.
The text says 'لم يكن له من يحل له جماعه' (has no one permissible for intercourse).
3
Determine the ruling
The obligation of istinja drops (sakat).
The text says 'سقط عنه الإستنجاء' (his istinja is dropped).
4
Understand the rationale
Because exposing the private part is only permissible for a spouse or mahram, and no such person is available.
The text: 'لأنه لا يحل فرجه إلا لذلك' (because his private part is not permissible except for that).
5
Apply the principle
This is a case of darurah (necessity) overriding a ritual obligation when fulfilling it would require a greater prohibition.
The ruling balances between the obligation of purification and the prohibition of exposing awrah to non-mahram.

Covering the Awrah During Istinja: Prohibition Overrides Sunnah
Ruling with proof: prohibition of uncovering awrah for istinja, supported by maxim and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on uncovering the awrah for istinja and explain why the prohibition takes precedence over performing a sunnah.

Core Idea
It is prohibited to uncover the awrah for istinja; preventing harm (dar' al-mafasid) takes precedence over achieving benefit (jalb al-masalih).

This lesson addresses a common tension: performing the sunnah of istinja (cleaning oneself) versus the obligation to cover the awrah. The Hanafi school emphatically rules that uncovering the awrah for istinja is haram, even if it means forgoing some thoroughness. We will explore the textual proofs and the legal maxim that underpin this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is uncovering the awrah specifically for the purpose of istinja. The matn states: 'لا يجوز كشف العورة للاستنجاء' – it is not permissible. Determine the hukm level from this phrasing.
The expression 'لا يجوز' in Hanafi fiqh typically indicates prohibition (tahrim), not mere dislike.
2
Locate the legal maxim
The hashiah cites the maxim 'درء المفاسد مقدم على جلب المصالح'. Understand the maxim: preventing harm is prioritized over bringing benefit. In this case, uncovering awrah is a harm (mafsadah) that outweighs the benefit of a more thorough istinja.
This maxim is a universal principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
3
Connect the hadith proofs
Two hadiths are quoted: 'ما نهيتكم عنه فاجتنبوه' (what I forbid, avoid) and a hadith about avoiding sin being better than worship. These establish that avoiding prohibitions is more important than performing commands.
The hadith about the mustard seed is narrated by Sahib al-Kashf; its authenticity is accepted for argumentation.
4
Understand the consequence
Allamah Nuh clarifies that uncovering awrah for istinja makes one a fasiq (transgressor) regardless of the amount of impurity or visibility. The ruling is absolute: one must not commit a haram to perform a sunnah.
This reinforces the principle that ends do not justify unlawful means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز كشف العورة للاستنجاء لحرمته، والفسق به فلا يرتكبه لإقامة السنة. قوله: (وما يكره فعله : أي حال قضاء الحاجة قوله فلا يرتكبه لإقامة السنة) لأن درء المفاسد مقدم على جلب المصالح غالباً، واعتناء الشرع بالمنهيات أشد بالمأمورات ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: ما نهيتكم عنه فاجتنبوه، وما أمرتكم به فافعلوا منه ما استطعتم وروي الترك ذرة مما نهى الله عنه أفضل من عبادة الثقلين» رواه صاحب الكشف قال العلامة نوح: المستنجي لا يكشف عورته عند أحد للإستنجاء فإن كشفها صار فاسقاً لأن كشف العورة حرام، ومرتكب الحرام فاسق سواء كان النجس مجاوزاً للمخرج أولا وسواء زاد على الدرهم أولا، ومن فهم من عبارتهم غير هذا فقد سها .اهـ.
It is not permissible to uncover the private part for istinja because of its prohibition, and transgression (fisq) is in it, so one should not commit it to perform a sunnah. His saying: 'and what is disliked to do' i.e. during relieving oneself. His saying: 'so he should not commit it to perform the sunnah' because warding off evils is given precedence over bringing benefits in most cases, and the Shari'ah's concern with prohibitions is stronger than with commands. Hence the Prophet said: 'What I forbid you, avoid it; and what I command you, do of it what you can.' And it is narrated that 'abandoning a mustard seed of what Allah forbade is better than the worship of the two heavy ones (mankind and jinn).' Reported by Sahib al-Kashf. Allamah Nuh said: The one performing istinja should not uncover his private part in front of anyone for istinja; if he uncovers it, he becomes a transgressor (fasiq) because uncovering the private part is haram, and the one who commits a haram is a fasiq, whether the impurity exceeds the exit or not, and whether it exceeds a dirham or not. Whoever understands from their statements otherwise has failed.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on covering the 'awrah (private parts) during istinja. The matn states that it is not permissible to uncover the 'awrah for istinja, as it is haram, and one should not commit a sin to perform a sunnah act. The hashiah explains the legal maxim: preventing harm takes precedence over achieving benefits. It supports this with the hadith 'What I forbid you, avoid it; what I command you, do as much as you can' and another hadith about the superiority of avoiding sins over worship. Allamah Nuh emphasizes that uncovering the 'awrah for istinja is fisq (transgression), regardless of the amount of impurity. The purpose of istinja (cleaning) does not justify the sin of exposing the 'awrah. This is a key principle in usul al-fiqh: dar' al-mafasid muqaddam 'ala jalb al-masalih.

Key Terms
درء المفاسد مقدم على جلب المصالح (dar' al-mafasid muqaddam 'ala jalb al-masalih): A legal maxim: preventing harm takes priority over achieving benefit. Applied here to prioritize covering awrah over performing sunnah.
فسق (fisq): Transgression; committing a major sin or persisting in minor sins. The one who uncovers awrah for istinja becomes a fasiq.

Istinja Dropped for the Incapacitated Sick Person
Ruling statement on sick person's istinja obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which istinja is dropped for a sick person and explain the underlying rationale.

Core Idea
Istinja is lifted when a sick person cannot clean himself and has no lawfully permissible helper.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi tradition regarding the obligation of istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself). While purifying oneself from impurity is generally required, the school recognizes an exemption when necessity and modesty intersect. Understanding this exception deepens appreciation for how the law accommodates human incapacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Istinja is the act of cleaning the private parts after using the toilet. The text rules that it is dropped (saqit) for a specific type of sick person.
2
Extract the conditions
Two conditions must both be present: (1) the person is unable to perform istinja themselves, and (2) there is no one who is lawfully permitted to see their private parts (i.e., spouse or mahram) to assist.
The second condition uses the phrase 'لہ حل جماعہ' indicating a person with whom intercourse is halal – a very specific category.
3
Analyze the ratio legis
The reason given is 'because his private part is not permissible except for that' – meaning exposing the 'awrah for non-mahram is prohibited. So the law prioritizes preventing sin over performing istinja when the two conflict.
4
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: a bedridden patient with no spouse and no mahram available. Istinja is dropped. If a mahram is available, the obligation remains – the helper must assist.
This shows the principle of 'necessity permits the prohibited' but only to the extent needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع في الخانية مريض عجز عن الاستنجاء ولم يكن له من يحل له جماعه سقط عنه الإستنجاء لأنه لا يحل فرجه إلا لذلك والله أعلم اهـ.
Branch: In al-Khaniyya: A sick person who is unable to perform istinja and has no one who is permissible for him to have intercourse, his istinja is dropped because his private part is not permissible except for that. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This is a separate ruling (far') from al-Khaniyya regarding a sick person. If a person is too ill to clean himself after relieving himself and he has no one who can lawfully see his private part (i.e., a spouse or mahram), then the obligation of istinja is waived. The reasoning is that his 'awrah cannot be exposed for this purpose except to a permissible person (like a spouse). This is an application of the principle of necessity: when removal of impurity is impossible without sin, the obligation is lifted.

Key Terms
فرع (far'): A branch or subsidiary ruling derived from principles.
استنجاء (istinja): Cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, usually with water.
عجز (ajaza): Inability or incapacity to perform an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Prohibition of Uncovering 'Awrah for Istinja' and Priority of Avoiding Haram
Ruling on prohibition of uncovering 'awrah for istinja' and principle of avoiding haram over sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on uncovering the 'awrah for istinja' and apply the principle that avoiding haram takes precedence over performing a sunnah.

Core Idea
Uncovering the 'awrah is haram even for istinja'; avoiding haram overrides performing sunnah.

Performing istinja' is a sunnah, but it cannot justify committing a prohibition. This lesson establishes that uncovering the 'awrah for istinja' is haram, and the Shari'ah principle 'warding off evils takes precedence over bringing benefits' governs this ruling. The text also provides a branch where istinja' is waived for a sick person to avoid exposing the 'awrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act being discussed: uncovering the 'awrah for the purpose of istinja'. Determine its hukm: haram, as stated explicitly in the text.
The text says 'لا يجوز كشف العورة للاستنجاء لحرمته' (it is not permissible to uncover the 'awrah for istinja' due to its prohibition).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith 'ما نهيتكم عنه فاجتنبوه، وما أمرتكم به فافعلوا منه ما استطعتم' (What I have forbidden you, avoid; what I have commanded, do as much as you can) and the statement that abandoning a mustard seed of haram is better than worship of both worlds.
These proofs emphasize the priority of prohibitions over commands.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the dalil proves the ruling: the imperative 'اجتنبوه' indicates prohibition (haram) in Hanafi usul. The additional narration reinforces that avoiding haram is superior to performing supererogatory acts.
The text explicitly applies the maxim 'درء المفاسد مقدم على جلب المصالح' (warding off evils takes precedence over bringing benefits).
4
Apply the branch case (far')
Consider the exemption: a sick person who cannot perform istinja' without uncovering their 'awrah and has no one whose seeing their 'awrah is permissible – istinja' is waived. This demonstrates that the prohibition of uncovering 'awrah supersedes the sunnah of istinja'.
This branch from al-Khaniyya shows the practical application of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يكره فعله لا يجوز كشف العورة للاستنجاء لحرمته، والفسق به فلا يرتكبه لإقامة السنة، ويمسح المخرج من تحت الثياب بنحو حجر وإن تركه صحت الصلاة بدونه. مس فيما يجوز به الاستنجاء قوله: (وما يكره (فعله : أي حال قضاء الحاجة قوله فلا يرتكبه لإقامة السنة) لأن : من اعتنائه درء المفاسد مقدم على جلب المصالح غالباً، واعتناء الشرع بالمنهيات أشد بالمأمورات ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: ما نهيتكم عنه فاجتنبوه، وما أمرتكم به فافعلوا منه ما استطعتم وروي الترك ذرة مما نهى الله عنه أفضل من عبادة الثقلين» رواه صاحب الكشف قال العلامة نوح: المستنجي لا يكشف عورته عند أحد للإستنجاء فإن كشفها صار فاسقاً لأن كشف العورة حرام، ومرتكب الحرام فاسق سواء كان النجس مجاوزاً للمخرج أولا وسواء زاد على الدرهم أولا، ومن فهم من عبارتهم غير هذا فقد سها .اهـ. فرع في الخانية مريض عجز عن الاستنجاء ولم يكن له من يحل له جماعه سقط عنه الإستنجاء لأنه لا يحل فرجه إلا لذلك والله أعلم اهـ.
And what is disliked to do: it is not permissible to uncover the 'awrah for istinja' due to its prohibition, and it is fisq (sin) so one should not commit it to establish the sunnah. And he wipes the exit from under the clothes with something like a stone, and if he leaves it, the prayer is valid without it. A question regarding what is permissible for istinja': His statement: 'And what is disliked to do' meaning at the time of relieving oneself. His statement: 'so one should not commit it to establish the sunnah' because, from his care, warding off evils takes precedence over bringing benefits most of the time, and the Shari'ah's concern with prohibitions is stronger than with commands. Hence he said, peace be upon him: 'What I have forbidden you, avoid it; and what I have commanded you, do of it what you are able.' And it is narrated: 'Abandoning a mustard seed of what Allah has forbidden is better than the worship of the thaqalayn (jinn and humans).' Narrated by the author of al-Kashf. Whoever understands from their expressions other than this has been negligent. End. A branch in al-Khaniyya: A sick person unable to perform istinja' and does not have someone whose seeing his 'awrah is permissible for him, istinja' is waived for him because his private part is not permissible except for that purpose. And Allah knows best. End.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage addresses the act of istinja' (cleaning after relieving oneself). It begins by stating that it is prohibited to uncover the 'awrah (private parts) for the purpose of istinja' because it is haram. Doing so constitutes fisq (sin) and should not be committed even to perform the sunnah act of istinja'. The commentator explains the underlying principle: avoiding evil takes precedence over bringing benefit, and the Shari'ah's prohibitions are more emphasized than commands. This is supported by the hadith 'What I have forbidden you, avoid; what I have commanded, do as much as you can.' The commentary further clarifies that uncovering the 'awrah for istinja' is sinful regardless of the amount of najis. Then a branch (far') from al-Khaniyya is mentioned: if a sick person cannot perform istinja' without uncovering his 'awrah and there is no one whose looking at his 'awrah is permissible (like a spouse), then istinja' is waived because exposing the 'awrah is only allowed for valid reasons like marriage. Thus, the preservation of the prohibition outweighs the sunnah of istinja'.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Private parts that must be concealed.
استنجاء (istinja'): Cleaning after relieving oneself.
درء المفاسد (dar' al-mafasid): Warding off evils, a legal maxim that takes precedence over bringing benefits.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness, disobedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) He should use a stone or cloth to wipe from under his clothes without exposure.

Key Takeaway
Avoiding the haram act of uncovering the 'awrah takes precedence over performing the sunnah of istinja'; if istinja' requires haram, it is waived.

The Pardoned Amount of Najis and Its Removal in Prayer
Ruling on najis amount and removal condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on the pardoned amount of najis to determine the validity of prayer and identify the condition for removal without uncovering the 'awrah.

Core Idea
Najis less than a dirham is pardoned; excess must be removed without uncovering the 'awrah.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the precise ruling on najis exceeding the pardoned amount. It explains the measurement method for solid and liquid najis, the obligation to remove it, and the exception when removal requires uncovering the 'awrah. Understanding this ruling is essential for evaluating the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of najis
Solid najis (mutajassida) is measured by weight; liquid najis (mai'a) is measured by area. The pardoned amount is less than a dirham for solids and a corresponding area for liquids.
Dirham ≈ 3.36 grams.
2
Determine the threshold for invalidation
Only the excess that has exited the body (alone) is considered. If this excess alone exceeds a dirham (by weight or area), prayer is invalid unless removed. What remains inside the exit is disregarded (saqit al-i'tibar).
The relied-upon position is that inside the exit is not counted.
3
Assess the ability to remove najis
If one can remove the najis without uncovering the 'awrah (to anyone who should not see it), removal is wajib. If removal requires uncovering, it is excused and prayer is valid even with the najis.
The prohibition of uncovering 'awrah takes precedence.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi refinement
Some claimed consensus on counting what is inside the exit, but the relied-upon position is that it is disregarded. This is the mufta bihi view supported by al-Hidayah.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تجاوزت النجاسة مخرجها، وزاد المتجاوز بانفراده على قدر الدرهم وزنا في المتجسدة ومساحة في المائعة لا تصح معه الصلاة الزيادته على القدر المعفو عنه إذا وجد ما يزيله من مائع أو ماء ويحتال لإزالته من غير كشف العورة عند من يراه تحرزاً عن إرتكاب المحرم بالقدر الممكن، وأما إذا لم يزد إلا بالضم لما في المخرج فلا يضر تركه لأنّ ما في المخرج ساقط الإعتبار. قوله: وزاد المتجاوز بانفراده) المعتمد قوله: (إذا وجد ما يزيله والأصلي معها ولا إعادة كما في الهداية قوله: ( ويحتال الخ) : أي إن أمكنه، وإلا فلا لأن كشف العورة حرام يعذر به في ترك طهارة النجاسة إذا لم يمكنه إزالتها من غير كشف قاله البرهان الحلبي : قوله عند من يراه المراد به من يحرم عليه جماعة ولو أمته المجوسية، والتي زوجها للغير لأنه لما حرم عليه وطؤهما حرم عليه نظرة إلى عورتهما، وكذا نظرهما إليه إذ متى حرم الوطء حرمت الدواعي إلا ما استثني كأمر أنَّه الحائض والنفساء وتمامه في حاشية الدر. قوله : لأنّ) ما في المخرج ساقط الاعتبار) : أي على المعتمد خلافاً لمن حكى عليه الإتفاق . هو
And if the najis exceeds its exit, and the excess alone exceeds the amount of a dirham by weight for solid najis and by area for liquid najis, prayer is not valid with it — the excess over the pardoned amount when there is something to remove it, whether liquid or water, and he must contrive to remove it without uncovering the 'awrah from one who sees him, as a precaution against committing the prohibited to the extent possible. But if it only increases by including what is inside the exit, then not removing it does not harm because what is inside the exit is disregarded. His statement: 'and the excess alone' is the relied-upon position. His statement: 'when there is something to remove it' and the original with it and no repetition as in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'and he contrives etc.': meaning if he is able, otherwise no, because uncovering the 'awrah is prohibited and is excused in leaving the purification of najis if he cannot remove it without uncovering. Said by Burhan al-Halabi. His statement: 'from one who sees him' refers to the one for whom looking at his 'awrah is prohibited, even his Magian slave woman and the one whose husband is another, because when intercourse with them is prohibited, looking at their 'awrah is prohibited, and similarly their looking at him, for whenever intercourse is prohibited, the means to it are prohibited except what is exempted like the woman in menstruation and postpartum. The complete discussion is in Hashiyat al-Durr. His statement: 'because what is inside the exit is disregarded': meaning on the relied-upon position, contrary to those who claim consensus on it.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage deals with the amount of najis that is excusable in prayer. The pardoned amount is less than a dirham (approx. 3.36 grams) for solid najis, and a corresponding area for liquid. If the najis exceeds that, it must be removed for prayer to be valid. However, the person must contrive to remove it without uncovering his 'awrah. If he cannot remove it without uncovering, he is excused because avoiding the haram takes precedence. The commentary clarifies that the excess is calculated alone, not including what is inside the exit, which is ignored. It also explains that the person to be avoided (when uncovering) is anyone whose seeing one's 'awrah is forbidden, such as non-mahram. The relied-upon position is that what is inside the exit is not counted, against a claim of consensus.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A unit of weight, approx. 3.36 grams.
متجسدة (mutajassida): Solid najis.
مائعة (mai'a): Liquid najis.
ساقط الاعتبار (saqit al-i'tibar): Disregarded, not taken into account.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Najis exceeding a dirham must be removed for prayer unless removal requires uncovering the 'awrah; inside the exit is disregarded.

Disliked Items for Istinja' and Their Validity
Listing of disliked items and validity ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which items are disliked for istinja', state the Hanafi ruling on their validity, and explain the evidence and cross-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Istinja' with bones or dung is valid but prohibitively disliked—the purpose of cleansing is achieved.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses the ruling on using certain items for istinja'. It lists bones, dung, and other materials as makruh, but crucially, the Hanafi school holds that using them is still valid. The proof is a hadith prohibiting their use, yet the school distinguishes between validity and dislike. Understanding this distinction is key to Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disliked Items
List all the items mentioned in the passage as disliked for istinja'.
Bones, dung, food, baked brick, small stones, charcoal, glass, gypsum, valuable cloth, cotton, and the right hand.
2
Distinguish the Level of Dislike
Separate the items into those that are prohibitively disliked (karahah tahrimiyyah) and those that are simply disliked (makruh tanzihi).
Bones and dung are karahah tahrimiyyah; others are makruh tanzihi.
3
Analyze the Proof
Examine the hadith cited and understand how the Hanafi school interprets its prohibition.
The prohibition form 'لا تستنجوا' indicates karahah tahrimiyyah, not haram, because the act still achieves its purpose.
4
Determine Validity
Note that despite the dislike, the Hanafi school considers istinja' with these items to be valid because the objective is cleansing.
The notice (tanbih) explicitly states validity.
5
Compare with Shafi'i
Identify the Shafi'i position and the practical consequence of the disagreement.
Shafi'i holds istinja' invalid; Hanafi holds valid. This affects whether one must repeat purification.

وتكرر، أو قاصر على قريب العهد الذي لم يطعمه أحد من الجن؟ والظاهر الثاني وإن كانت الكراهة في الجميع لأن العلة تعتبر في الجنس، وأفاد الحديث الشريف أن الجن يأكلون وقيل : رزقهم الشم ولا خلاف إنهم مكلفون، عقاب قوله: (وفحم لتلويثه)، ولما روي أنه لما قدم وفد الجن على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، قالوا: يا رسول الله إنه أمتك أن يستنجوا بعظم أو روث، أو حممة فإن الله تعالى جعل لنا فيها رزقاً فنهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك والحممة كرطبة الفحم وما احترق من الخشب، أو العظام ونحوهما، وقوله : رزقاً : أي انتفاعاً لهم بالطبخ والدفا، والإضاءة فيكره الإستنجاء بذلك لافساده، ولا ينافي هذا الحديث ما تقرر إن And it is disliked to perform istinja' with a bone or dung because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Do not perform istinja' with dung or bones, for they are food of your brothers from the jinn. So if they find them, the bone becomes as if it had not been eaten, and they eat it, and the dung becomes barley and straw for their animals, as a miracle for the Prophet. And the prohibition indicates karahah tahrimiyyah (close to haram). (And food for a human or animal due to disgrace and waste, and he forbade it, peace be upon him.) And baked brick (ajur) because it does not clean the place and harms it, so it is disliked. And small stones (khazaf) because it does not clean and soils the hand. And charcoal because it dirties. And glass and gypsum because they harm the place. And something valuable like silk cloth and cotton because it wastes wealth and performing istinja' with it brings poverty. And it is disliked to perform istinja' with the right hand because of his statement: 'If one of you urinates, do not wipe his private part with his right hand; and if he goes to the lavatory, do not wipe with his right hand; and if he drinks, do not drink in one breath except due to an excuse.' With the left hand, he should perform istinja' by pouring water from a servant or from water. His statement: 'The bone becomes as if it had not been eaten' meaning the bone on which the name of Allah was mentioned because of the hadith: every bone on which the name of Allah is mentioned will fall into your hands or become flesh? Is this realized even after a long time and repetition, or is it limited to recent ones that no jinn have eaten? The second is apparent even though the dislike is in all because the cause is considered for the genus. The blessed hadith teaches that jinn eat, and some say their provision is smelling, and there is no disagreement that they are accountable, only about their reward: from Imam Abu Hanifa there is suspension, and also that their reward is protection from punishment as per verse (61:6), which does not entail reward. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ibn Abi Layla say they have reward as they have punishment. His statement: 'And charcoal because it dirties' and the narration that when a delegation of jinn came to the Prophet, they said: O Messenger of Allah, your nation should not perform istinja' with bone, dung, or charred wood (hamma) for Allah has made for us therein provision. So the Messenger forbade that. Hamma is like moist charcoal and what is burned of wood or bones etc. His statement: 'provision' meaning benefit for them in cooking, warming, and lighting. So istinja' with that is disliked because it spoils. This hadith does not contradict what is established, that this was made for them by the Prophet, and it implies its existence for them before him, for the meaning is 'made for us provision by your making them for us' for it is from Allah. His statement: 'So he does not wipe with his right hand' al-Ayni said in Sharh al-Bukhari: the prohibition is for tanzih (dislike) according to the majority because of two reasons: one is to elevate the status of the right hand, the other that if he handles najis with it, perhaps when handling food he will remember what his right hand handled, and his nature will recoil. Contrary to the Zahiris. The dislike is in both types of istinja'. His statement: 'he performs istinja' by pouring with a servant' this is contrary to what the exception gives, for it indicates the absence of dislike with the right hand in case of an excuse, and if an excuse occurs for the right hand, istinja' is dropped as in al-Hamawi from al-Muhit. A notice: If one performs istinja' with these disliked items, al-Qut' said in Ghayat al-Bayan: If he disobeys the prohibition and performs istinja' with that, does it suffice? According to us (Hanafis) yes, according to al-Shafi'i no, because the purpose is cleansing, and it has been achieved.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage lists various items that are disliked (makruh) for use in istinja'. The primary ones are bones and dung, based on a hadith that these are food for the jinn. The prohibition is at the level of karahah tahrimiyyah (close to haram). Other items include food (even for animals), baked brick, small stones, charcoal, glass, gypsum, valuable items like silk and cotton, and using the right hand. The commentary explains each: the hadith about bones and dung, the fact that jinn are created and have needs, and the miracle of the Prophet. The ruling on the right hand is that it is disliked for istinja' due to respect for the right hand, and the hadith prohibits it. However, if there is an excuse, the dislike is removed, and one may use the right hand. The notice (tanbih) at the end clarifies that even if one uses these disliked items, the istinja' is valid according to the Hanafi school because the object is cleanliness, which has been achieved, contrary to al-Shafi'i who considers it invalid.

Key Terms
روث (rawth): Dung, animal excrement.
عظم (adhm): Bone, specifically animal bone.
كراهة التحريم (karahah al-tahrim): Prohibitively disliked, close to haram.
آجر (ajur): Baked brick or tile.
خزف (khazaf): Small stones or pottery shards.
فحم (fahm): Charcoal.
يد يمنى (yad yumna): Right hand.

Key Takeaway

Disliked Materials for Istinja and the Hadith of Jinn
Ruling on makruh materials for istinja with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the materials considered makruh tahrimi for istinja in the Hanafi school, state the evidence from the hadith of the jinn delegation, and explain the usul principle that a prohibition (nahi) indicates karahah tahrimi.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prohibition of using bones and dung for istinja yields karahah tahrimi, not haram, because the hadith is zanni al-thubut.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi explains the ruling on various materials that are disliked for cleaning after relieving oneself. He cites the well-known hadith of the jinn delegation, where the jinn requested Muslims not to use bones, dung, or coal—these are provisions for them. The Hanafi school classifies this prohibition as makruh tahrimi, a level just short of haram, due to the nature of the evidence. We will examine the list of prohibited materials, explore the proof from the Sunnah, and understand why the ruling is not outright haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is istinja (cleaning private parts). The ruling is that using certain materials (bones, dung, etc.) is makruh tahrimi.
The prohibition level is based on the hadith's zanni transmission.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof is the hadith of the jinn delegation: 'Every bone on which Allah's name is mentioned falls into your hands or becomes meat' and the explicit request that the ummah not use bone, dung, or coal.
A second hadith about not using the right hand is also cited.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's prohibition (nahi) is absolute. In Hanafi usul, nahi mutlaq indicates impermissibility (hurmah). Since the hadith is ahad, the level is lowered from haram to makruh tahrimi.
If the evidence were qati, the ruling would be haram; here it is zanni al-thubut.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'is consider istinja with these materials invalid if done intentionally, while Hanafis hold it valid but sinful. There is also a theological dispute on whether jinn actually eat or just smell, and whether they are rewarded.
The disagreement on jinn reward does not affect the fiqh ruling.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is makruh tahrimi, and the prohibition applies to all listed materials. The act of istinja remains valid.
The passage also discusses an exception for using the right hand in case of excuse.

الجنس، وأفاد الحديث الشريف أن الجن يأكلون وقيل : رزقهم الشم ولا خلاف إنهم مكلفون، وإنما الخلاف في إثابتهم فروي عن الإمام التوقف وروي عنه أن إثابتهم إجارتهم من العذاب لقوله تعالى: (ويجركم من عذاب أليم
