يستنجوا بعظم أو روث، أو حممة فإن الله تعالى جعل لنا فيها رزقاً فنهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك والحممة كرطبة الفحم وما احترق من الخشب، أو العظام ونحوهما، وقوله : رزقاً : أي انتفاعاً لهم بالطبخ والدفا، والإضاءة فيكره الإستنجاء بذلك لافساده، ولا ينافي هذا الحديث ما تقرر إن ذلك كان يجعل النبي ، ا ا ، وهذا يقتضي ثبوته لهم قبله فإنَّ المعنى جعل لنا فيها رزقاً بسبب جعلك إياها لنا فإنَّه عن الله عز وجل. قوله : (فلا يتمسح بيمينه) قال العيني في شرح البخاري والنهي للتنزيه عند الجمهور لأنه لمعنيين أحدهما رفع قدر اليمين والآخر أنه لو باشر بها النجاسة ربما يتذكر عند مناولة الطعام ما باشرت يمينه، فينفر طبعه عن ذلك خلافاً للظاهرية، والكراهة في الإستنجاء بقسميه. قوله: (فيستنجي بصب خادم هذا خلاف ما يعطيه الاستثناء فإنه يفيد عدم الكراهة باليمين حال العذر وهو . فإن حصل عذر باليمين سقط الاستنجاء كما في الحموي عن المحيط.
Your brethren from the jinn increased. When they find them (bones and dung), the bone becomes as if it was not eaten, so they eat it, and the dung becomes barley and straw for their animals as a miracle for the Prophet. The prohibition indicates karahah tahrimi (dislike approaching impermissibility). (And food of a human or animal, due to disrespect and waste, and he [the Prophet] prohibited it, peace be upon him.) (And baked brick [آجر]) with a long 'a', dammah on the jim, and shaddah on the ra', Persian arabicized; it means 'al-tub' in Egyptian dialect, also called 'ajur' on the pattern of fa'ul; it is burnt clay; it does not clean the place and harms it, so it is disliked. (And small pebbles [خزف]) small stones; they do not clean and soil the hand. (And coal [فحم]) because it dirties, (and glass and plaster) because they harm the place. (And something valuable) because it is precious, like a silk rag (and cotton) because it wastes wealth, and performing istinja with it causes poverty. (And) it is disliked to perform istinja (with the right hand) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'When one of you urinates, let him not touch his penis with his right hand; when he goes to the toilet, let him not wipe himself with his right hand; when he drinks, let him not drink in one breath.' Except with an excuse, using the left, he performs istinja with the pouring of a servant or with water. His saying: (The bone becomes as if it was not eaten): meaning the bone over which Allah's name was mentioned, as in the hadith: 'Every bone on which Allah's name is mentioned falls into your hands or becomes meat.' Is this realized even if its time is remote and repeated, or is it specific to recent ones that no jinn has eaten? The apparent is the second, though dislike is general because the cause is considered in type. The noble hadith indicates that jinn eat; it is said their provision is by smell. There is no dispute that they are obligated, but there is disagreement on their reward: It is reported that Imam Abu Hanifa withheld; it is also reported that their reward is being spared from punishment as per the verse: 'And He will spare you from a painful punishment' (61:6) which does not entail reward. And Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ibn Abi Layla said: They have reward just as they have punishment. His saying: (And coal because it dirties), and due to the narration that when the delegation of jinn came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, they said: 'O Messenger of Allah, forbid your nation from performing istinja with a bone, dung, or coal, for Allah has made provision for us in them.' So the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prohibited that. Coal is like a fresh piece of charcoal or anything burnt from wood or bones, etc. His saying 'provision' means benefit for them in cooking, heating, and lighting. So istinja with them is disliked because it spoils. This hadith does not contradict what was established that the Prophet made them [provision]? And this requires that it was established for them before him, because the meaning is: He made provision for us in them because You made them for us, from Allah Almighty. His saying: (So let him not wipe himself with his right hand) Al-Ayni said in Sharh al-Bukhari: The prohibition is for tanzih (dislike) according to the majority, due to two reasons: one, honoring the right hand; the other, that if he handles impurity, he might remember when handling food what his right hand touched, thus his nature being repulsed, contrary to the Zahiris. The dislike is for both types of istinja. His saying: (He performs istinja with the pouring of a servant) This contradicts what the exception gives, as it indicates no dislike with the right hand in case of an excuse. So if there is an excuse with the right hand, istinja is dropped, as in al-Hamawi from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on the disliked materials for istinja. The author lists several items that are makruh tahrimi (close to impermissible) to use for cleaning after relieving oneself. These include bones and dung because they are food for the jinn, food for humans or animals (due to waste), baked bricks, small pebbles, coal, glass, plaster, valuable items like silk, cotton (due to wasting wealth), and using the right hand. The prohibition level is deduced from the hadith where the Prophet explicitly forbade these, and the Hanafi principle that a prohibition implies karahah tahrimi. The commentary then discusses the hadith about the jinn delegation, explaining that bones and dung are provisions for the jinn, and that the Prophet's prohibition is based on that. There is a discussion among scholars about whether jinn eat actual food or only smell, and whether they are rewarded. Abu Hanifa reportedly withheld on reward, while Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Malik, and Ibn Abi Layla affirm reward. The commentary also explains the prohibition of using the right hand, which is for tanzih (dislike) according to the majority, honoring the right hand and avoiding psychological aversion. An exception is made for an excuse, where using the right hand is permissible. The passage ends with a note that if there is an excuse, the obligation of istinja may be dropped.

Key Terms
كراهة التحريم (karāhat al-taḥrīm): A level of prohibition in Hanafi fiqh less than haram, based on zanni evidence.
الاستنجاء (al-istinjā'): Cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself using water or solid purifiers.
نَهْي (nahy): A prohibition; in usul, it indicates impermissibility unless there is evidence to lower the level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using a coal for istinja?
A) It is haram and invalidates the purification.
B) It is makruh tahrimi, and the purification is still valid.
C) It is mubah, and there is no problem.
D) It is sunnah, as coal is clean.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that using bones, dung, coal, and other specified materials for istinja is makruh tahrimi, based on the hadith of the jinn delegation, and the act remains valid if performed.

Validity of Istinja with Disliked Materials: The Hanafi Objective-Based Approach
Ruling on the validity of istinja using makruh materials – a Hanafi vs. Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja with makruh materials and explain why the prohibition does not invalidate the act, relying on the principle of maqsad (objective).

Core Idea
Istinja with makruh material is valid because the objective (cleaning) is achieved; prohibition does not nullify the act.

In this note, al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi position on a specific case: performing istinja (cleaning after relieving oneself) using materials that are legally disliked (makruh). The key question is whether the prohibition on the material renders the purification invalid. The Hanafi answer, grounded in a teleological view of the act, is that as long as the objective of cleaning is accomplished, the act suffices. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the prohibition
The act is istinja (cleaning the private parts after using the toilet). The prohibition is against using certain materials (like baked brick or bones) that are makruh tanzihi or tahrimi for istinja.
The text refers to 'these disliked materials' mentioned earlier in the chapter.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on validity
According to the text, 'indana na'am' (according to us, yes) meaning the istinja is valid (yujzih) and fulfills the obligation of purification.
The Hanafi position is that the act is legally sufficient despite the prohibition.
3
Identify the opposing school's position
The text states 'wa ind al-Shafi'i la' (according to al-Shafi'i, no), meaning the Shafi'i school considers the istinja invalid when done with makruh materials.
The Shafi'i reasoning is likely that the prohibition (nahi) in acts of worship causes invalidity (ifsad).
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof: 'al-maqsud al-tanqiyah wa qad hasalat' (the objective is cleaning, and it has been achieved). The prohibition is on the material, not on the act of cleaning itself; hence the objective overrides the minor prohibition.
This is a classic example of Hanafi reliance on maqasid (objectives) in ibadat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: According to Hanafis, the person's purification is valid, and they may pray without repeating istinja. According to Shafi'is, the istinja must be repeated with permissible materials.
Note: Hanafis still consider using the makruh material a sin, but it does not affect the validity of purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : لو استنجى بهذه المكروهات فقال : في غاية البيان عن الأقطع فإن ارتكب النهي واستنجى بذلك هل يجزيه فعندنا نعم وعند الشافعي لا لنا أن المقصود التنقية، وقد حصلت،
Note: If one performs istinja with these disliked materials, he said in Ghayat al-Bayan from al-Aqta': 'If he violates the prohibition and performs istinja with that, does it suffice him?' According to us, yes; according to al-Shafi'i, no. For us, the objective is cleaning, and it has been achieved.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether istinja performed with makruh materials is valid. The Hanafi position is that it is valid because the underlying objective (tanqiyah, cleaning) has been achieved. The Shafi'i position, according to the text, is that it is not valid. The reasoning for the Hanafi view is purely teleological: the purpose of istinja is purification, and since the cleaning has occurred, the act suffices. The note is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi, citing an earlier work (Ghayat al-Bayan) to clarify that despite the prohibition, the ritual obligation is fulfilled.

Key Terms
إجزاء (ijzā'): The quality of being legally sufficient; that the act fulfills the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs istinja with baked brick (آجر) despite the prohibition, what is the Hanafi ruling on the validity of his purification?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated with water.
B) It is valid but the person is sinful for using the disliked material.
C) It is valid and praiseworthy because he saved water.
D) It is invalid and requires a dam (penalty).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the objective of an act (maqsad) can override a minor prohibition; istinja with makruh materials is valid because cleaning is achieved.

Etiquettes of Entering the Toilet: Recommended Acts and Their Proofs
Critical refinement of toilet etiquettes with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) actions when entering the toilet according to the Hanafi school, cite the supporting hadiths, and distinguish the sunnah order of basmalah before isti'adhah.

Core Idea
Entering with left foot, covering head, and saying basmalah then isti'adhah is sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, not wajib.

This lesson explores the recommended etiquettes for entering the toilet as derived from hadith and explained in the Hanafi school. While these actions are not obligatory, they bring spiritual protection and follow the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding the proper order and the reasoning behind each act helps the believer adhere to the sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the actions mentioned in the base text: entering with left foot, covering the head, and reciting the isti'adhah (seeking refuge).
The text uses 'استحباباً' indicating recommendation.
2
Examine the proofs
Two hadiths are cited: one about saying Bismillah as a barrier, and one about saying the isti'adhah in the outhouse. Identify the evidence type (Sunnah ahad).
The hadiths are transmitted individually (ahad).
3
Determine the hukm level
The term 'استحباباً' and the context show the actions are mustahabb (sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah), not obligatory.
In Hanafi usul, commands for protection imply recommendation unless specified otherwise.
4
Note the refinement of order
The commentator clarifies that basmalah precedes isti'adhah, contrary to common practice in Quran recitation. Cite Ibn Hajar and the Ya'muri hadith.
The usual order in recitation is isti'adhah then basmalah; here it is reversed.
5
Apply in practice
For a built toilet, recite the dhikr before entering. For open spaces, recite at the moment of commencing to uncover. If forgotten, recite silently in the heart.
This distinction is based on the nature of the location.

عورته ويقدم تسمية الله تعالى على الإستعاذة لقوله عليه السلام ستر ما بين أعين الجن وعورات بني آدم إذا دخل أحدكم الخلاء أن يقول باسم الله ولقوله عليه السلام: إن الحشوش مختضرة، فإذا أتى فليقل أعوذ بالله من الخبث والخبائث والشيطان معروف، وهو من شطن يشطن إذا بعد، ويقال فيه شاطن وشيطن ويسمى بذلك كل متمرد من الجن والإنس والدواب لبعد غوره، في الشر، شاط يشيط إذا هلك فالمتمرد هالك بتمرده ويجوز أن يكون مسمى بفعلان لمبالغته في إهلاك غيره، والرجيم مطرود باللعن والحشوش جمع الحش بالفتح والضم بستان النخيل في الأصل، ثم استعمل في موضع قضاء الحاجة واحتضارها صد بني آدم بالأذى، وقيل من وإنما ورد النهي لمعنى في غيره اهـ فصار كما لو صلى السنة في أرض مغصوبة كان آتياً بها مع إرتكاب النهي نهر وهو مخالف لما بحثه أخوه قوله: (ويدخل الخلاء) سمي به للإختلاء فيه، وأصله المكان للخالي الذي لا شيء فيه ثم كثر استعماله حتى تجوز به عن ذلك، وأما بالقصر فهو الحشيش الرطب الواحدة خلاة مثل حصا وحصاة وفي الحديث لا يختلي خلاها وبكسر الخاء والمد عيب في الإبل كالحران في الخيل قوله (المتوضأ) : أي محل الوضوء اللغوي، وهو النظافة، ولو اقتصر على قوله : والمراد الخ كغيره لكان أولى. قوله: (برجله اليسرى) : أي ويخرج باليمنى عكس المسجد فيهما قوله : (يحضره الشيطان) الأولى جعله تعليلاً آخر كما فعله السيد قوله : (ولهذا يستعيذ : أي لأجل حضور الشيطان قال في المصباح: استعدت بالله وعدت به معاذاً وعياذاً اعتصمت وتحصلت، وتحصنت، واستجرت به، والتجأت إليه اهـ. قوله : (قبل دخوله الأولى التفصيل وهو إن كان المكان معداً لذلك يقول قبل الدخول وإن كان غير معدّ له كالصحراء ففي أوان الشروع كتشمه الثياب مثلاً قبل كشف العورة، وإن نسي ذلك أتى به في نفسه لا بلسانه قوله : ( ويقدم تسمية الله تعالى الخ) ما ذكره لا يفيد التقديم، فالأولى ما قاله ابن حجر : السنة هنا تقديم التسمية على التعوذ عكس المعهود في التلاوة ولحديث اليعمري : إذا دخلتم الخلاء فقولوا : باسم الله أعوذ بالله من الخبث والخبائث، وإسناده على شرط مسلم اهـ قال بعض الفضلاء بالإكتفاء بأحدهما يحصل أصل السنة، والجمع أفضل. قوله : (من الخبث جمع خبيث، وهو المؤذي من الجن، والشياطين يروى بضم الباء وسكونها تخفيفاً، ولا وجه لإنكار الخطابي التسكين، وإن اشتبه لفظه حينئذ بلفظ المصدر قوله : (والخبائث) من إناثهم قوله : ( لبعد غروه في الشر) المراد لشدة قبحه في الشر. قوله : (بالفتح) هو الأكثر قوله : (بستان النخيل في الأصل) وكانوا يتغوطون بين النخيل قبل اتخاذ الكنف في البيوت، ثم كني به عن موضع قضاء الحاجة مطلقاً.
He said: (And one enters the khala') with a long vowel; it means the place of relieving oneself. (With his left foot) initially, covering his head as a recommended act out of honor for the right foot, because it is a filthy place and the devil attends it. (And) for this (he seeks refuge), i.e., he protects himself from the accursed devil before entering and before uncovering his private parts. And he mentions the name of Allah Almighty before seeking refuge, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'A barrier between the eyes of the jinn and the private parts of the children of Adam when one of you enters the toilet is that he says: In the name of Allah.' And due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The outhouses are frequented, so when one comes, let him say: I seek refuge with Allah from the male and female devils.' And the devil is known, and it is from shatana (to become distant), and it is said shaytan and shaytan, and every rebellious being from jinn, humans, and animals is called by that due to the depth of his evil. shata yashitu means to perish, so the rebellious one is perished by his rebellion, and it is permissible that it is named fa'lan for his exaggeration in destroying others. Al-rajim (the accursed) is driven out by curse. Al-hushush is plural of al-hash (with fath and damm), originally a palm garden, then used for the place of relieving oneself and its presence, blocking the children of Adam with harm. And it was said: the prohibition came for a meaning in other than it, so it becomes like if one prayed the sunnah in usurped land, he performed it while committing the prohibition. It is contrary to what his brother researched. His statement: (And one enters the khala'), so called because of being alone there, and its origin is the empty place with nothing in it, then its usage increased until it was metaphorically used for that. As for with qasr, it is fresh grass, one is khalat like hasa and hasat, and in the hadith: 'No one should pick its khalat.' With kasr of kha and madd, it is a defect in camels like being restive in horses. His statement: (al-mutawadda') i.e., the place of linguistic wudu', which is cleanliness. If he had sufficed with saying 'the intended meaning etc.' like others, it would have been better. His statement: (with his left foot) i.e., and he exits with his right, opposite of the masjid in both. His statement: (the devil attends it) the first is to make it another reason as did al-Sayyid. His statement: (and for this he seeks refuge) i.e., due to the presence of the devil. He said in al-Misbah: I seek refuge with Allah and seek protection with him, meaning I take shelter and fortify myself. His statement: (before entering) the first is detail: if the place is prepared for that, he says it before entering; if it is not prepared, like the desert, then at the time of commencing, like when he smells his clothes, etc., before uncovering the private parts. If he forgets that, he says it within himself, not with his tongue. His statement: (and he mentions the name of Allah Almighty before seeking refuge, etc.) what he mentioned does not establish precedence, so the better is what Ibn Hajar said: The sunnah here is to mention the name before seeking refuge, opposite of what is usual in recitation, and due to the hadith of al-Ya'muri: 'When you enter the toilet, say: In the name of Allah, I seek refuge with Allah from the male and female devils,' and its chain is upon the condition of Muslim. He said: Some virtuosi said, 'Suffice with one of them; the basis of sunnah is achieved, and combining is better.' His statement: (al-khubth) is plural of khabith, and it is the harmful male jinn and devils; it is narrated with damm of the ba and sukun as a lightening, and there is no basis for al-Khattabi's denial of sukun, even if its form then resembles the verbal noun. His statement: (wal-khaba'ith) are their females. His statement: (due to the depth of his evil in evil) means the intensity of his ugliness in evil. His statement: (with fath) is the more common. His statement: (palm garden originally) and they used to relieve themselves among palm trees before taking latrines in houses, then it was used metaphorically for the place of relieving oneself absolutely.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the etiquettes of entering the toilet. The commentator first explains the base text: one should enter with the left foot, cover the head recommendably (istihbaban), and seek refuge (isti'adhah) before entering. The reasons given are honor for the right foot and because the devil attends such places. The isti'adhah is specifically before uncovering the private parts. The procedure includes mentioning Allah's name (basmalah) before the isti'adhah, supported by two hadiths. The first hadith states that saying 'Bismillah' creates a barrier between jinn and human private parts. The second hadith orders saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-khubthi wal-khaba'ith' when entering the outhouse. The commentator then discusses lexical and terminological meanings: 'khala'' is the place of solitude, 'hushush' are palm gardens originally used for defecation. He clarifies that the sunnah order is basmalah then isti'adhah, contrary to common practice in Quran recitation (where isti'adhah precedes basmalah). He cites Ibn Hajar and a hadith from al-Ya'muri. The passage also addresses details: if the toilet is not a built structure (like the desert), the dhikr is said at the moment of commencing uncovering, not before. If one forgets, he recites silently. The commentary ends by explaining the variant readings of 'al-khubth' (singular or plural) and that it refers to male evil jinn, while 'al-khaba'ith' refers to their female counterparts. The overall ruling is that these actions are mustahabb (recommended) and not obligatory; but omitting them is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khalā'): The place of relieving oneself (toilet), derived from the meaning of solitude.
الحشوش (al-ḥushūsh): Plural of al-hashsh, originally a palm garden, later metaphorically used for any place of relieving oneself.
الخبث والخبائث (al-khubth wal-khabā'ith): Al-khubth refers to male evil spirits (jinn/shayatin), and al-khaba'ith refers to their female counterparts.
استعيذ (ista'īdh): To seek refuge and protection, specifically from the accursed devil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on covering the head when entering the toilet?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah)
C) Sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah (mustahabb)
D) Makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)

Key Takeaway
Entering the toilet with left foot, covering the head, and reciting 'Bismillah' before 'A'udhu billahi' are mustahabb (sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah) acts that provide protection from devils.

The Prohibition of Facing the Qibla During Relieving Oneself
Establishes the ruling on facing qibla and its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla while relieving oneself, identify the hadith proof, and apply the exception for necessity.

Core Idea
Facing or turning your back to the qibla when relieving oneself is prohibitively disliked, even inside buildings.

This passage from al-Tahtawi establishes the core Hanafi position on facing the qibla during elimination. While the act is not haram, it is makruh tahrimi based on the explicit hadith and the principle of reverence for the qibla direction. The commentary clarifies that this applies universally, even in built structures, with only narrow exceptions for genuine necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act in question? Facing or turning one's back to the qibla during elimination. The hukm level is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'When you come to defecate, do not face the qibla nor turn your back to it, but face east or west.' This is a sahih hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
The hadith is general and applies to both open areas and buildings.
3
Understand the scope
The ruling applies even in buildings. The phrase 'وَلَوْ فِي الْبُنْيَانِ' (even in buildings) explicitly extends the prohibition to built environments.
The commentator refutes the idea that a wall provides a barrier, comparing it to prayer where the wall does not negate facing the qibla.
4
Note the exception
If the wind forces one to face a certain direction due to necessity, it is not disliked. If forced, one should choose turning the back over facing, as facing is more disrespectful.
The exception is based on the principle of necessity (darura).
5
Distinguish from other acts
This ruling is specific to elimination. Intercourse facing the qibla is permissible (though khilaf al-awla), as there is no prohibition reported for that act.
This distinction is important to avoid over-applying the prohibition.

كان ذيله مرخى ويستثنى من المنع على ظاهر الرواية ما لو كانت الريح وهو ظاهر ان تهب عن يمين القبلة، أو شمالها فإنهما لا يكرهان للضرورة، وإذا اضطر إلى أحدهما ينبغي أ يختار الإستدبار لأن الإستقبال أقبح، فتركه أدل على التعظيم أفاده القسطلاني، والمنلا علي في شرح المشكاه قوله : (حال) قضاء الحاجة) خرج حال الجماع لما نقله ابن أمير حاج عن النووي في شرح مسلم يجوز الجماع مستقبل القبلة في الصحراء، والبنيان هذا مذهبنا ومذهب أبي حنيفة، وأحمد وداود واختلف فيه أصحاب ما لك فجوزه ابن القاسم، وكرهه ابن حبيب، والصواب الجواز فإنّ التحريم إنما يثبت بالشرع، ولم يرد فيه نهي، والأولى أن يقال: إنه خلاف الأولى لما سيأتي . قوله: (واختار التمرتاشي عدم الكراهة) : أي التحريمية وإلا فهو ترك أدب كمد الرجل إليها كما في الحلبي قوله : (وهو بإطلاقه منهي ) : أي الحديث مطلق فيفيد الكراهة في البنيان، فالأولى للمؤلف أن يقول وهو بإطلاقه يقتضي النهي، ولو في البنيان قال : في غاية البيان لأن النهي لتعظيم الجهة، وهو موجود فيهما فالجواز في البنيان أن كان لوجود الحائل فالحائل موجود أيضاً في الصحراء كالجبال والأودية ولأن المصلي في البيت يعتبر مستقبل القبلة، ولا تجعل الحائط حائلاً، فكذا إذا كشف العورة في البيت لا تجعل الحائط حائلاً اهـ. قوله : ( وانحرف إجلالاً لها قيد الإجلال لا بد منه في المغفرة وبحث في النهر وجوبه وقال في النهاية : فإن لم يفعل لم يكن به بأس .اهـ. قال الحلبي : وأنه لم يجب لأنه وقع معفواً عنه للسهو، وهو فعل واحد اهـ ويظهر أن المراد الإنحراف عن الجهة لأنه متى كان فيها عد
And the qada' (relieving oneself) is that their abode becomes due to the exit of waste, and he sits leaning on his left side because it is easier for elimination of waste, and he spreads his legs apart, and does not speak except for necessity because it is hated on that occasion. And it is prohibitively disliked to face the qibla with the private parts during relieving oneself, and they differed about facing it for purification, and al-Tamartashi chose non-dislike. And (it is disliked) to turn one's back to it, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'When you come to defecate, do not face the qibla nor turn your back to it, but face east or west.' And it is absolutely forbidden, even in buildings. And if one sits facing it forgetfully, then remembers and turns away out of reverence for it, he should not get up from his place until he is forgiven, as narrated. His statement: (They lie in wait for the children of Adam with harm) i.e., they wait and watch them, it is a masdar added to its object, if read with sukun, or with fath and intended as masdar. He said in al-Qamus: 'He watched, watching and watching, meaning he awaited.' And it is possible that with fath it is the plural of raqib. He said in al-Qamus: 'al-rasad (with harakat) means the watchers.' And that is because it is a place where the private parts are uncovered and the name of Allah is not mentioned. His statement: (And it is prohibitively disliked absolutely to face the qibla) Multiple narrations from the Imam regarding this matter: it is reported that he forbade it – this is the narration as in al-Fath; the second is absolute permission; the third is dislike of facing only; the fourth is dislike of turning the back as well, unless his garment is hanging long. And from the prohibition according to the apparent narration is excepted when the wind is blowing from the right or left of the qibla; then these are not disliked due to necessity, and if one is forced to one of them, he should choose turning the back because facing is worse, so leaving it is more indicative of reverence. This was stated by al-Qastalani and al-Mulla 'Ali in Sharh al-Mishkat. His statement: (During relieving oneself) excludes the state of intercourse, as Ibn Amir Hajj narrated from al-Nawawi in Sharh Muslim: 'It is permissible to have intercourse facing the qibla in the desert and buildings. This is our madhhab and the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, Ahmad, and Dawud. And the companions of Malik differed: Ibn al-Qasim permitted it, while Ibn Habib disliked it. The correct view is permissibility, for prohibition is only established by law, and no prohibition has been reported regarding it. It is better to say that it is against what is preferable (khilaf al-awla) as will come.' His statement: (And al-Tamartashi chose non-dislike) i.e., the prohibitively disliked, otherwise it is abandoning etiquette like stretching the foot towards it as in al-Halabi. His statement: (And it is absolutely forbidden) i.e., the hadith is absolute and indicates dislike even in buildings. So it is better for the author to say: 'It requires prohibition even in buildings.' He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'Because the prohibition is for reverence of the direction, and that exists in both. So permissibility in buildings would be due to the presence of a barrier, but the barrier also exists in the desert like mountains and valleys, and because the one praying in a house is considered facing the qibla, and the wall is not considered a barrier. Likewise, if one uncovers his private parts in a house, the wall is not considered a barrier.' His statement: (And turned away out of reverence for it) The condition of reverence is necessary for forgiveness. And it was researched in al-Nahr: its obligation. And it was said in al-Nihaya: 'If he does not do so, there is no harm.' Al-Halabi said: 'It is not obligatory because it is excused due to forgetfulness, and it is a single action.' And it appears that the intended meaning is turning away from the direction because whenever he is in it, he is counted.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the ruling of facing the qibla while relieving oneself. The commentator begins with additional etiquettes: sitting leaning on the left side, spreading legs, not speaking except for necessity. Then he addresses the core ruling: it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to face the qibla with the private parts during elimination, and also to turn one's back to it, based on the hadith 'When you come to defecate, do not face the qibla nor turn your back to it.' The hadith is general (mutlaq) and applies even in buildings. The commentator then presents the multiple narrations (riwayat) from Abu Hanifa: 1) prohibition absolute (the relied-upon narration in al-Fath), 2) absolute permissibility, 3) dislike only for facing, 4) dislike for both facing and turning back unless the garment is hanging long. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is prohibition (makruh tahrimi). However, there are exceptions: if the wind blows from the right or left of the qibla, it is not disliked due to necessity; if forced, one should choose turning the back as facing is more severe. The passage also distinguishes between relieving oneself and sexual intercourse: intercourse facing the qibla is permissible (ja'iz) but khilaf al-awla (contrary to what is better). This is the Hanafi position, shared with Ahmad and Dawud, while some Malikis differ. The commentator refutes the idea that a wall in a building serves as a barrier making it permissible, arguing that the reverence for the qibla direction remains. For one who forgetfully faces qibla and then turns away out of reverence, it is recommended (not obligatory) to remain seated until forgiveness; the obligation is debated but the stronger view is it is not obligatory due to the excuse of forgetfulness.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbāl al-qiblah): Facing the direction of the Ka'ba with the private parts while relieving oneself.
كراهة تحريمية (karāhah taḥrīmiyyah): A classification of disliked action that is close to haram; requires leaving it and avoiding, but not as severe as haram.
الرواية (al-riwāyah): A transmitted narration of a ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa, differing from the well-known zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on turning one's back to the qibla while relieving oneself in a built toilet?
A) Permissible (ja'iz)
B) Makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
C) Makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
Facing or turning the back to the qibla during elimination is makruh tahrimi even inside buildings, based on the general hadith.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Facing the Qibla
Discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four narrations from Abu Hanifa on facing the qibla, identify the relied-upon position, and explain the tarjih reasoning.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa has four narrations; the relied-upon one prohibits facing and turning the back.

This passage delves into the multiple narrations (riwayat) attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the ruling on facing the qibla during elimination. The commentator presents these variant reports and explains why the prohibition (man') is the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah). The lesson also touches on related issues, such as the permissibility of intercourse facing the qibla and the refutation of the barrier argument.

Guided Path
1
Count the narrations
List the four narrations from Abu Hanifa as mentioned in the text: (1) absolute prohibition, (2) absolute permission, (3) dislike of facing only, (4) dislike of both facing and turning back unless the garment is long.
These narrations reflect different ijtihads within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the first narration: absolute prohibition (makruh tahrimi). This is the position recorded in al-Fath and is consistent with the majority of the six books.
The other narrations are considered weak or less authoritative.
3
Understand the tarjih
The prohibition is preferred because it aligns with the hadith's general prohibition and the principle of reverence for the qibla direction. The other narrations are overruled by the explicit and general nature of the hadith.
Tarjih is conducted by later scholars like al-Qastalani and al-Mulla Ali.
4
Explore the exception
The exception for wind-driven necessity is consistent across narrations. If forced, turning the back is recommended over facing, as facing is more disrespectful.
This shows that even within the prohibition, there is room for necessity.
5
Compare with other acts
Distinguish between elimination and intercourse. Intercourse facing the qibla is permissible (khilaf al-awla) because no prohibition is reported. This highlights that the prohibition is specific to elimination.
The text also refutes the barrier argument using the analogy of prayer.

Prohibited Acts and Places While Relieving Oneself
Lists acts and places that are makruh tahrimi when relieving oneself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prohibited places and acts while relieving oneself, identify the proofs, and distinguish between levels of prohibition (makruh tahrimi, tanzihi, haram).

Core Idea
Avoid the two that cause cursing: relieving oneself on paths and in shades – and other places like water, holes, and under trees.

The text from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details a comprehensive list of actions and locations that are detested during relieving oneself. These rulings are grounded in hadith and reasoning about harm, respect for Allah's signs, and public courtesy. Understanding these nuances is essential for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each listed item, state the act (e.g., urinating in water) and the hukm level (makruh tahrimi, tanzihi, haram).
2
Locate the dalil
Cite the hadith or reasoning given for each prohibition. E.g., the hadith of la'innan for path and shade.
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof yields the ruling. For example, the imperative 'ittaqu' implies prohibition; the harm to people is the illa.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For water, distinguish between stagnant (makruh tahrimi) and running (makruh tanzih), and the opinion that small stagnant water is haram.
Some scholars detail based on quantity.
5
Apply the distinction
Understand that not all prohibitions are equal; some are haram, some makruh tahrimi, some tanzihi.

بخلاف ما إذا كان جامداً قوله : (ولو جارياً ينبغي أن يكون في الراكد مكروهاً تحريماً لأنه غاية ما يفيده حديث لا يبولن أحدكم في الماء الدائم وفي الجاري مكروهاً تنزيهاً فرقا بينهما بحر من بحث المياه قال بعض الحذاق والظاهر التفصيل في الراكد ففي القليل منه يحرم لأنه ينجسه، وتنجيس الطاهر حرام، وفي الكثير يكره تحريماً، والتغوط فيه كالبول، بل أقبح، وعن ابن حجر يكره قضاء الحاجة في الماء بالليل مطلقاً خشية أن يؤذيه الجن لما قيل أن الماء بالليل مأواهم قوله : ( وبقرب بتر ونهر وحوض)، ومصلى عيد وقافلة، وخيمة، وبين الدواب كما في الدرر، وغيره لأنه يكون سبباً للعن، وينبغي أن يلحق بذلك مصلي الجنازة كذا بحثه بعضهم، وهو ظاهر قوله : ( والظل) قال الأبهري: موضع الشمس في الشتاء كالظل في الصيف، وهذا إذا كان مباحاً، وأما إذا كان مملوكاً فيحرم فيه قضاء الحاجة بغير إذن مالكه كما في شرح المشكاة، وتقييده بالذي يجلس فيه يفيد أنه لا كراهة فيما لا حاجة إليه. قوله : (والحجر) بضم الجيم، وإسكان الحاء الخرق في الأرض، والجدار لقوله : لا يبولن أحدكم في حجر» رواه أبو داود والنسائي. قوله : (لأذية ما فيه) اعتباره مصدراً مضافاً إلى مفعوله، وإلى فاعله وقيل إنها مساكن الجن، فقد نقل أن سعد بن عبادة الخزرجي بال في حجر بأرض حوران فقتله الجن. قوله : ( والطريق) ولو في ناحية منها قوله : (اتقوا اللاعنين) : أي اللذين هما سبب اللعن والشتم غالباً فكأنهما لاعنان من باب تسمية الحال فاعلاً مجازاً، وقيل اللاعن بمعنى الملعون قوله لإتلاف الثمر)
And it is detested to hold a child towards the Qibla for urination because both [sun and moon] are great signs, and the direction from which the wind comes because it returns to him and contaminates him. And it is detested to urinate or defecate in water, even if running, and near a well, river, or basin, and in the shade in which one sits, and in a hole because of the harm in it, and on the road, and in a graveyard due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Avoid the two that cause cursing.' They said: What are the two that cause cursing, O Messenger of Allah? He said: 'The one who relieves himself on the path of people or in their shade.' And under a fruit-bearing tree because it destroys the fruit. His saying: (And it is detested to hold a child...) Everything that an adult is detested to do, it is detested to do to a small child. So it is detested to hold him while he relieves himself towards the Qibla, or towards the two moons (sun and moon), etc. And it is haram to feed him or clothe him with something haram, and the sin is on the adult who does that to him. His saying: (And it is detested to face the sun and the moon directly) The absolute expression of detestation necessitates tahrim, and qualifying with 'directly' indicates that if he is in a hidden place and their disk is not visible, it is not detested, unlike the Qibla. And this is the text of al-Allamah Jibril in Sharh Muqaddimah Abi al-Layth. Mentioning 'facing' indicates that turning one's back to them is not detested. His saying: (because they are two great signs) And it is said: because of the angels that accompany them, as in al-Siraj and others. His saying: (and the direction from which the wind comes) This is apparent for facing, and similarly turning the back if his excrement is very liquid because the cause of urine exists in it, unlike if it is solid. His saying: (even if running) It should be that in stagnant water it is makruh tahrimi because that is the limit of what the hadith 'Let none of you urinate in standing water' indicates. In running water, it is makruh tanzih, differentiating between them as in al-Bahr from the discussion of waters. Some experts said: the obvious is detail in stagnant water: in a small amount it is haram because it contaminates it, and contaminating pure water is haram; in a large amount it is makruh tahrimi. And defecating in it is like urination, even worse. And from Ibn Hajar, it is detested to relieve oneself in water at night absolutely, fearing that the jinn may harm him, because it is said that water is the abode of jinn at night. His saying: (and near a well, river, and basin) and an Eid prayer ground, a caravan, a tent, and among animals, as in al-Durar and others, because it is a cause for cursing. And it should be added to that the janazah prayer ground, as some discussed, and it is apparent. His saying: (and the shade) Al-Abhari said: the place of the sun in winter is like the shade in summer. This applies if it is permissible (mubah). But if it is owned, then relieving oneself there without the owner's permission is haram, as in Sharh al-Mishkat. Qualifying it with 'in which one sits' indicates that there is no detestation for places not needed. His saying: (and the hole (hajar)) with damm on the jim and sukun on the ha, meaning a crevice in the ground or a wall, due to his saying: 'Let none of you urinate in a hole,' reported by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. His saying: (because of the harm in it) It is considered a verbal noun connected to its object and to its subject. And it is said they are the dwellings of jinn, for it is reported that Sa'd ibn Ubadah al-Khazraji urinated in a hole in the land of Hawran, and the jinn killed him. His saying: (and the road) even if on its side. His saying: (avoid the two that cause cursing) i.e., the two actions that are often the cause of cursing and insult, so they are as if they are 'cursers' metaphorically. And it is said 'the one who curses' means 'the one who is cursed.' His saying: (because it destroys the fruit)
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on prohibited acts and places while relieving oneself. The main text enumerates several actions and locations that are makruh tahrimi: (1) Holding a child towards the Qibla for urination—since it is detested for an adult, it is likewise detested to do to a child. Feeding a child haram food or clothing them in haram is itself haram, with sin on the adult. (2) Facing the sun or moon directly while relieving oneself—this is makruh tahrimi because they are great signs of Allah associated with angels. The detestation applies only when the disk is visible; if one is in a covered place, it is not detested, unlike the ruling for the Qibla where the direction is respected even without seeing the Kaaba. Turning one's back to them is not detested. (3) The direction from which the wind comes—facing the wind is detested because it may blow back and contaminate the person. Similarly, turning one's back is also detested if one's excrement is very liquid. (4) Urinating or defecating in water—stagnant water is makruh tahrimi, running water is makruh tanzih. Some scholars detail that in a small amount of stagnant water it is haram because it contaminates the water; in large amounts it is makruh tahrimi. Defecating is worse. Ibn Hajar adds that it is detested at night due to fear of jinn. (5) Near a well, river, basin, Eid prayer ground, caravan route, tent, or among animals, because such places invite cursing by people who use them. (6) In the shade where people sit—if the shade is on public land (mubah), it is detested; if on private property, it is haram without the owner's permission. The qualification 'in which one sits' means that if the shade is not used for sitting, there is no detestation. (7) In a hole (hajar) in the ground or wall, as there may be harm or jinn dwellings; a hadith prohibits urinating in holes. (8) On the road, even at the side, and in graveyards—this is based on the hadith 'Avoid the two that cause cursing,' i.e., relieving oneself on people's paths or in their shade. (9) Under a fruit-bearing tree because it may destroy the fruit or harm the tree. Each prohibition is supported by a hadith or sound reasoning. The overall theme is to avoid actions that cause disrespect, harm, or annoyance to others or to sacred entities.

Key Terms
اللاعنان (al-lā'innān): The two actions that cause cursing, i.e., relieving oneself on a path or in shade, resulting in people cursing the perpetrator.
الحجر (al-ḥajar): A hole, crevice in the ground or wall; also means stone but here a specific meaning.
استقبال عين الشمس والقمر (istiqbāl 'ayn al-shams wa al-qamar): Facing the sun or moon directly (the disk visible). If the sun/moon is not in sight, not detested.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the hadith 'Avoid the two that cause cursing', what are the two actions?
A) Urinating in water and under a tree
B) Relieving oneself on the path of people or in their shade
C) Facing the sun and moon while relieving oneself
D) Urinating in a hole and near a well

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits relieving oneself in places that harm people, disrespect sacred signs, or violate property rights, with rulings ranging from haram to makruh tanzihi.

Disliked Actions While Relieving Oneself
Listing makruh acts during istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five makruh acts during qada' al-hajah and distinguish between makruh tanzih and makruh tahrimi based on the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Many common actions while relieving are disliked; knowing their degree preserves worship and avoids sin.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed rulings of the Hanafi school on actions that are disliked (makruh) while one is relieving oneself (qada' al-hajah). The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi lists several acts with commentary explaining their degrees based on evidence. Understanding these rulings helps a Muslim maintain proper adab and avoid harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each action mentioned, note whether it is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) or makruh tahrimi (close to haram).
The commentary specifies degrees; e.g., facing sun/moon is tahrimi, facing wind is tanzihi.
2
Examine the reason or evidence
Look for the basis given for the dislike, such as a hadith, harm, or respect for Allah's signs.
The hadith of 'the two cursers' is cited for road and shade.
3
Note exceptions
Some actions become permissible with an excuse, like standing for urination due to back pain.
The exception is explicitly stated.
4
Apply to real scenarios
Consider how these rulings apply to modern situations, such as using a toilet with a phone containing Quran.
The ruling on entering with something that has Allah's name applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
الطبراني مرفوعاً، ويكره إمساك الصبي نحو القبلة للبول (و) يكره (إستقبال عين الشمس والقمر) لأنهما آيتان عظيمتان ومهب الريح) لعوده به فينجسه (و) يكره أن يبول أو يتغوط في الماء) ولو جارياً ويقرب بئر ونهر وحوض (والظل) الذي يجلس فيه (والحجر) لأذية مافيه (والطريق) والمقبرة لقوله عليه السلام اتقوا اللاعنين قالوا وما اللاعنان يا رسول الله قال : الذي يتخلى في طريق الناس أو ظلهم وتحت شجرة مثمرة) لإتلاف الثمر (و) يكره (البول) (قائماً لتنجسه غالباً إلا من عذر كوجع بصلبه ويكره في محل التوضؤ لأنه يورث الوسوسة ويستحب دخول الخلاء بثوب غير الذي يصلي فيه وإلا يحترز ويتحفظ من النجاسة، ويكره الدخول للخلاء ومعه شيء مكتوب فيه إسم الله أو قرآن ونهى عن كشف عورته قائماً
The book of purification. Al-Tabarani as marfu': It is disliked to hold a child facing the qibla for urination. And it is disliked to face the sun or moon, because they are two great signs. And (it is disliked to face) the direction of the wind, because it may return and soil him. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, even if running, and near a well, river, or basin. And (it is disliked) in the shade where one sits, and in a hole (hajar) because of harmful creatures, and on the road, and in a graveyard, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Avoid the two cursers.' They said: What are the two cursers, O Messenger of Allah? He said: 'He who relieves himself in the road people use or in their shade.' And (it is disliked) under a fruit-bearing tree, because of wasting fruit. And it is disliked to urinate standing, because it generally soils him, except for an excuse such as back pain. And it is disliked in the place of wudu, because it causes waswas. And it is recommended to enter the toilet with a garment other than that in which one prays, otherwise one should be careful and guard against impurity. And it is disliked to enter the toilet with something on which is written the name of Allah or the Quran. And he forbade uncovering one's private parts while standing.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi enumerates various disliked (makruh) actions related to relieving oneself (qada' al-hajah). The rulings are based on the Hanafi school, with commentary explaining the reasoning and occasional distinctions. The author first mentions that it is makruh to hold a small child facing the qibla when the child urinates, because the child is not accountable but the adult commits a disliked act. Then, facing the sun or moon directly is makruh tahrimi (close to haram) because they are great signs of Allah, though facing away is not disliked. Facing the wind is also disliked if it causes soiling. Urinating or defecating in water, even running, is disliked; for stagnant water it is tahrimi, for running water tanzihi. Similarly, near wells, rivers, basins, and places like the Eid prayer ground or camps is disliked due to causing curses. The shade used by people is disliked, and a 'hajar' (hole in the ground) is disliked because it houses harmful creatures or jinn. Roads and graveyards are disliked based on the hadith of the 'two cursers.' Under a fruit tree is disliked because it wastes fruit. Urinating standing is disliked due to soiling, except for an excuse like back pain. Urinating in the place of wudu is disliked because it leads to waswas (whispers of Shaytan). The author recommends entering the toilet with a different garment to avoid impurity. It is disliked to enter with anything bearing Allah's name or Quranic verses, based on the Prophet removing his ring with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah' engraved. Uncovering the private parts while standing is forbidden until one is close to the ground. The commentary by al-Tahtawi refines these rulings by specifying degrees of karahah, citing earlier authorities, and noting exceptions.

Key Terms
قضاء الحاجة (qada' al-hajah): Relieving oneself, i.e., urinating or defecating.
اللاعنان (al-la'anayn): Two acts that cause cursing: relieving in road or shade.
الوسوسة (al-waswasah): Whispers of Shaytan leading to obsessive doubts about purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Haram under all circumstances
D) Recommended to avoid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a detailed list of disliked actions during istinja, with varying degrees of karahah based on evidence, helping believers maintain purity and respect.

Ruling on Urinating While Standing: Dislike, Proof, and Exceptions
Explains dislike of urinating standing with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on urinating while standing, identify the proof for dislike, and explain the exception for a valid excuse.

Core Idea
Urinating while standing is disliked (makruh tanzih) not haram, but permissible with an excuse like pain.

In the Hanafi school, urinating while standing is considered a disliked act due to the risk of soiling oneself and its crudeness. However, this ruling is not absolute; it is tempered by a clear exception for those with a valid excuse, such as physical pain or necessity. This lesson unpacks the textual evidence, the range of scholarly opinions within the Hanafi school, and the practical implications for daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
What is the act? What is the default hukm stated in the matn?
The matn states 'yukrahu' – it is disliked.
2
Extract the underlying reason
Why is it disliked? The text mentions 'li-tanajjusihi' (because it causes impurity).
Also consider adab (crudeness).
3
Examine the exception
What qualifies as an excuse? The matn gives back pain; the commentary adds hadith of the Prophet standing due to a wound.
The exception is key to understanding the school's approach.
4
Compare conflicting opinions
Al-Tahawi said no harm; some said the prohibition is tahrimi. How does the school weigh these?
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf acknowledged.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
What is the relied-upon position? The majority holds it as makruh tanzih, permissible with excuse.
This is the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكره (البول) (قائماً لتنجسه غالباً إلا من عذر كوجع بصلبه قال في شرح المشكاة قيل: النهي للتنزيه، وقيل للتحريم، وفي البناية قال الطحاوي: لا بأس بالبول قائماً .اهـ. قوله : (لتنجسه غالباً) : أي لتنجس الشخص به ولأنه الجفاء كما أنه عليه الصلاة ورد. قوله: (إلا) من عذر) روي مكاناً والسلام بال قائماً لجرح في باطن ركبته لم يتمكن معه من العقود، وقيل لأنه لم يجد طاهراً للعقود لامتلاء الموضع بالنجاسات، وقيل لوجع كان بصلبه الشريف فإن العرب تستشفي لوجع الصلب بالبول قائماً كما قاله الشافعي وقال الغزالي في الإحياء : قال زين العرب : أجمع أربعون طبيباً على أن البول في الحمام قائماً دواء من سبعين داء.
Urinating standing is disliked because it generally causes impurity except with an excuse like pain in his back. He said in Sharh al-Mishkat: It is said the prohibition is for desirability, and it is said for prohibition. And in al-Binayah, al-Tahawi said: There is no harm in urinating standing. End. His saying: 'because it generally causes impurity' means the person becoming impure by it and because it is crudeness as the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated. His saying: 'except with an excuse' - it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) urinated standing due to a wound in the inner part of his knee which prevented him from squatting, and it is said because he did not find a clean place to squat due to the area being filled with impurities, and it is said due to pain in his noble back, for the Arabs used to treat back pain by urinating standing as al-Shafi'i said. And al-Ghazali said in Ihya: Zayn al-Arab said: Forty physicians agreed that urinating in the bath while standing is a cure for seventy diseases.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage begins the book of Taharah and discusses the ruling of urinating while standing. The matn states it is disliked (makruh) because it generally leads to soiling, with an exception for a genuine excuse like back pain. The commentary expands by noting a difference of opinion: some say the prohibition is merely tanzihi (disliked not sinful), others say it is tahrimi (prohibited). Al-Tahawi even says there is no harm. The proof for dislike is that it is crude and can cause impurity, as the Prophet (PBUH) indicated. The exception comes from his own action when he had a wound or unclean place. Medical benefits are also noted. In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that it is makruh tanzihan, but permissible with an excuse.

Key Terms
يكره (yukrahu): It is disliked; a ruling indicating that avoiding it is better but not sinful.
البول قائماً (al-bawl qa'iman): Urinating while standing; a specific act considered undesirable unless necessary.
لتنجسه (li-tanajjusihi): Because it causes impurity to himself (by splashing).
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): A level of dislike where the act is better avoided but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling for urinating while standing?
A) It is haram under all circumstances.
B) It is disliked (makruh tanzih) unless there is an excuse.
C) It is completely permissible without any dislike.
D) It is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Urinating standing is makruh tanzih (disliked) in the Hanafi school, but becomes permissible with a valid excuse such as pain or necessity.

Dislike of Urinating in the Place of Wudu
Explains the legal ruling and its cause-based exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on urinating in the place of wudu and identify the condition that removes the dislike.

Core Idea
Urinating in the wudu place is disliked because it causes waswas; if no waswas arises, the ruling changes.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in taharah: urinating in the place where one normally performs wudu or ghusl. The Prophet (PBUH) warned against it due to the waswas (obsessive doubts) it generates. However, the ruling is not absolute — modern bathrooms with drains may remove the cause, altering the hukm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the act being ruled upon (urinating in the place of wudu) and the hukm level (makruh tanzih).
The text states 'yuqra' (disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'None of you should urinate in his bathing place...'.
The dalil is the direct prohibition from the Prophet (PBUH).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the imperative form indicates dislike, and the stated cause (waswas) shows the underlying reason.
The phrase 'inna 'ammata al-waswasi minhu' explicitly links the act to waswas.
4
Note the condition that removes the ruling
Identify the exceptions: if no splash can occur or there is a drain so no urine remains, the dislike is lifted because no waswas is caused.
This shows the ruling is cause-based (ta'lili) and not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويكره في محل التوضؤ) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يبولن أحدكم في مستحمه، ثم يغتسل فيه، أو يتوضأ فإن عامة الوسواس منه، قال ابن ملك لأن ذلك الموضع يصير نجساً فيقع في قلبه وسوسة بأنه هل أصابه منه رشاش أم لا اهـ؟ حتى لو كان بحيث لا يعود منه رشاش أو كان فيه منفذ بحيث لا يثبت فيه شيء من البول لم يكره البول فيه إذ لا يجره إلى الوسوسة حينئذ لأمنه من عود الرشاش إليه في الأول، ولظهر أرضه في الثاني بأدنى ماء طهور يمر عليها كذا في شرح المشكاة.
His saying: (And it is disliked in the place of wudu) because of his saying (PBUH): 'None of you should urinate in his bathing place, then wash or perform wudu in it, for most waswas (doubts) come from that.' Ibn Malik said because that place becomes impure, so doubt arises in his heart whether any splash hit him or not. So if it is such that no splash returns to him, or there is a drain so that no urine remains, then urinating there is not disliked because it does not lead to waswas, due to safety from splash in the first case, and the ground becoming pure with the least pure water passing over it in the second, as stated in Sharh al-Mishkat.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This sub-section discusses the ruling of urinating in the place where one normally performs wudu. It is disliked based on a hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) warning that it leads to waswas (obsessive doubts) about impurity. Ibn Malik explains that the place becomes impure, causing anxiety about splash. However, if the design prevents splash or if there is a drain that removes urine, the dislike is removed because no waswas arises. This shows that the ruling has a clear cause (waswas), and when the cause is absent, the ruling changes. In practice, many toilets today have drains, so this dislike may not apply, but it is still better to avoid.

Key Terms
الوسوسة (al-waswasah): Doubts and obsessive thoughts about impurity or validity of worship.
مستحمه (mustahammihi): Place of bathing; includes place of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked to urinate in the place of wudu?
A) It is physically impure.
B) It leads to waswas (obsessive doubts) about impurity.
C) It is disrespectful to water.
D) It wastes water.

Key Takeaway
Urinating in the place of wudu is disliked only when it may cause waswas; if no splash or residue remains, the ruling lifts.

Ruling on Using a Separate Garment for the Toilet
Discusses recommendation of separate toilet garment and critiques it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on having a special garment for the toilet and explain the difference between the two Hanafi views.

Core Idea
Using a special garment for the toilet is not a confirmed practice of the Prophet; the stronger view is that it is not recommended.

This passage discusses whether it is recommended (mustahabb) to use a separate garment for entering the toilet. The matn from al-Siraj states it is recommended, but the commentator from al-Nihayah rejects this, citing that the Prophet (PBUH) and the Caliphs did not do so. Understanding this difference helps clarify the Hanafi approach to deriving rulings from practice versus textual recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, note that al-Siraj recommends a separate garment. Second, al-Nihayah says it is not good and narrates that Zayn al-Abidin abandoned it after learning the Prophet did not do it.
The passage directly contrasts two Hanafi sources.
2
Understand the evidence for each
The recommendation is based on the idea of preserving the purity of the prayer garment. The critique is based on the lack of prophetic practice (fi'l) and the example of the Companions.
The evidence for the latter is stronger because it relies on the Sunnah.
3
Determine the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi authorities (like al-Tahtawi) side with al-Nihayah, considering it not recommended. Therefore, the operative ruling is that it is not mustahabb to prepare a special garment.
Students should note that this is a case of ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويستحب دخول الخلاء بثوب غير الذي يصلي فيه) هذا ما في السراج لكن قد ذكر في باب الإنجاس عن النهاية ما نصه ولا يحسن لأحد إعداد ثوب لدخول الخلاء، وروي أن محمد بن علي زين العابدين تكلف لبيت الخلاء ثوباً ثم تركه وقال : لم يتكلف لهذا من هو خير مني يعني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، والخلفاء رضي الله تعالى عنهم اهـ ومثله في غاية البيان.
His saying: (And it is recommended to enter the toilet with a garment other than the one in which he prays) This is what is in al-Siraj, but it is mentioned in the chapter on impurities from al-Nihayah: It is not good for anyone to prepare a garment for entering the toilet. And it is narrated that Muhammad ibn Ali Zayn al-Abidin made a garment for the toilet, then left it and said: 'One better than me did not bother with this,' meaning the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) and the Caliphs (may Allah be pleased with them). End. And similar is in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents two views regarding having a special garment for the toilet. The matn (from al-Siraj) recommends it, but the commentator from al-Nihayah says it is not good, citing that the Prophet (PBUH) and the Caliphs did not do so. Zayn al-Abidin initially prepared one but left it after realizing the Prophet did not. Thus, while it is not prohibited, it is not considered an established sunnah. The Hanafi school generally leans towards simplicity; it is fine to use the same garment if it is protected from impurity. The recommendation may apply if one's prayer garment is easily soiled.

Key Terms
يستحب (yustahabbu): It is recommended; doing it is rewarded, not doing it is not sinful.
خلاء (khala'): Toilet; place for relieving oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the stronger view regarding a separate garment for the toilet?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is recommended and the Prophet did it.
C) It is not recommended because the Prophet did not do it.
D) It is disliked.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet (PBUH) did not use a special garment for the toilet; therefore, it is not recommended to do so.

Carrying Allah's Name into the Toilet: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on carrying something with Allah's name into toilet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering the toilet with an object bearing Allah's name, explain the proof from the hadith, and identify the conditions that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Entering the toilet with Allah's name is disliked unless the name is covered.

This lesson addresses a common concern: Is it permissible to carry a ring, phone, or any item with Allah's name into the toilet? The Hanafi school bases its ruling on the Prophet's action of removing his ring. We will explore the proof, the degree of prohibition, and how covering or necessity changes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon. Here, it is entering the toilet (khala) while carrying something with Allah's name or Quran. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked).
The dislike is due to disrespect, not because the act is forbidden.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited by the author. The hadith of Anas in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi reports that the Prophet removed his ring before entering the toilet because it bore the words 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'.
The hadith text: 'كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا دخل الخلاء نزع خاتمه'
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's action indicates it is better to remove or conceal items with sacred names. The Hanafis see this as a recommendation (nadb), not an obligation (wujub).
Some scholars argue from the same hadith that it is obligatory, but the majority Hanafi view is dislike, not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize the difference of opinion. Al-Tibi and others consider it obligatory; Hanafis (and Ibn Hajar) consider it recommended/disliked. The Hanafi mufta bihi is makruh tanzih.
This difference affects whether one sins by not removing the item.
5
Apply exceptions and conditions
Determine when the dislike is removed. If the name is covered (e.g., in a pocket, or ring bezel turned inward), there is no dislike. Necessity also permits it, though caution is better.
The ruling also extends to items like water jugs or basins with sacred writing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويكره الدخول للخلاء ومعه شيء مكتوب فيه إسم الله أو قرآن) لما روى أبو داود والترمذي عن أنس قال: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا دخل الخلاء نزع خاتمه : أي لأن نقشه محمد رسول الله قال الطيبي : فيه دليل على وجوب تنحية المستنجي اسم الله تعالى واسم رسوله والقرآن ،اهـ، وقال الأبهري: وكذا سائر الرسل اهـ، وقال ابن حجر استفيد منه أنه يندب لمريد التبرز أن ينحى كل ما عليه معظم من اسم الله تعالى، أو نبي، أو ملك فإن خالف كره لترك التعظيم ،اهـ، وهو الموافق لمذهبنا . كما في شرح المشكاة قال بعض الحذاق ومنه يعلم كراهة استعمال نحو ابريق في خلاء مكتوب عليه شيء من ذلك اهـ وطشت تغسل فيه الأيدي، ثم محل الكراهة إن لم يكن مستوراً فإن كان في جيبه فإنه حينئذ لا بأس به، وفي القهستاني عن المنية الأفضل أن لا يدخل الخلاء وفي كمه مصحف إلا إذا اضطر ونرجو أن لا يأثم بلا اضطرار اهـ وأقره الحموي، وفي الحلبي الخاتم المكتوب فيه شيء من ذلك إذا جعل فصه إلى باطن كفه قيل لا يكره والتحرز أولى اهـ.
His saying: (And it is disliked to enter the toilet with something written on it the name of Allah or Quran) because Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi narrated from Anas: The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) used to remove his ring when entering the toilet, that is because its engraving was 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. Al-Tibi said: In this is evidence for the obligation of removing the name of Allah and His Messenger and the Quran. Al-Abhari said: And similarly for other messengers. Ibn Hajar said: From this it is understood that it is recommended for one intending to relieve himself to remove everything on which there is a venerated name of Allah, a prophet, or an angel; if he does not, it is disliked due to leaving respect. This is consistent with our madhhab. As in Sharh al-Mishkat, some astute scholars said that from this it is known that it is disliked to use a jug in the toilet on which something like that is written, and a basin for washing hands. Then the place of dislike is if it is not covered; if it is in his pocket, then there is no harm. In al-Qahistani from al-Munya: It is better not to enter the toilet with a mus-haf in his sleeve unless compelled, and we hope he does not sin without compulsion. End. And al-Hamawi affirmed it. And in al-Halabi: The ring with something written on it, if he turns the bezel to his palm, it is said not disliked, but caution is better.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of entering the toilet while carrying something that bears the name of Allah, the Prophet, or Quranic verses. It is disliked based on the hadith that the Prophet (PBUH) removed his ring before entering. The scholars differ on whether it is obligatory or recommended to remove it. The Hanafi school follows the view that it is disliked (makruh) if not necessary, but if the object is covered (e.g., in a pocket), it is not disliked. For a ring, turning the bezel inward also avoids dislike. The ruling extends to any object with sacred writing, like a water jug. However, if there is a genuine need (like preserving the object), it is permissible. The key is to avoid disrespect.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike; an act that is better to avoid but not sinful.
التعظيم (al-ta'zim): Reverence; showing respect to sacred names and objects.
الخاتم (al-khatam): Ring; specifically the Prophet's ring with engraving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when is it NOT disliked to carry a ring with Allah's name into the toilet?
A) When the ring is made of silver.
B) When the engraving is hidden by turning the bezel inward.
C) When the ring is worn on the right hand.
D) It is always disliked.

Key Takeaway
Carrying Allah's name into the toilet is disliked (makruh tanzih) unless covered or necessary, based on the Prophet's practice.

Prohibition of Uncovering Awrah While Standing for Toilet
Ruling on delaying uncovering until near ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on uncovering awrah while relieving oneself and identify the proof from the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
Do not uncover your awrah until you are close to the ground – the Prophet's practice prohibits unnecessary exposure.

This lesson examines the ruling on uncovering the private parts while relieving oneself. The Hanafi position relies on the hadith of Anas, which shows the Prophet's careful avoidance of exposure. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and the difference of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is uncovering the awrah while standing to relieve oneself before nearing the ground. The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh), with a difference of opinion between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzih; the mufta bihi is makruh tahrimi.
The ruling applies whether in the desert or in a building.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith of Anas (radiyallahu 'anhu) narrated by Tirmidhi: 'When the Messenger of Allah wanted to relieve himself, he would not lift his garment until he came close to the ground.' This is a sound (hasan) hadith.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted as evidence.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's action of delaying lifting the garment until near the ground indicates that uncovering earlier, without necessity, is not permitted. The absence of necessity before nearing the ground makes early uncovering blameworthy.
The principle is that uncovering the awrah without necessity is prohibited; necessity (like fear of soiling) allows earlier lifting but only to the extent of need.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
There are two opinions: some consider it makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), others makruh tanzih (lightly disliked). The preferred opinion (mufta bihi) is makruh tahrimi because the hadith explicitly discourages early uncovering.
The difference also applies to uncovering after finishing; the author's wording includes that scenario.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Al-Tahtawi notes the two opinions and leans toward prohibition due to the strength of the hadith. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, and the mufta bihi is makruh tahrimi.
This ruling is specific to the act of relieving oneself; for general uncovering without need, the ruling is similar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ونهي عن كشف عورته قائماً) : أي لقضاء الحاجة حتى يدنو من الأرض تحرزاً عن كشف العورة بغير ضرورة لقول أنس رضي الله تعالى عنه : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أراد الحاجة لم يرفع ثوبه حتى يدنو من الأرض رواه الترمذي بسند حسن قال الأبياري في شرح الجامع الصغير : محله ما لم يخف التنجس والأرفع بقدر الحاجة اهـ وقال الطيبي : يستوي فيه الصحراء والبنيان لأن كشف العورة لا يجوز إلا عند الحاجة يعني الضرورة، ولا ضرورة قبل القرب من الأرض، وعدم الجواز أحد قولين في الخلوة عندنا وشمل كلام المصنف كشفها بعد الفراغ فيكره إما تحريماً أو تنزيهاً على الخلاف في كشف العورة في الخلوة، ويستحب غسل يده بعد الفراغ وإن ظهرت بطهارة المحل مبالغة في التنظيف.
His saying: (And prohibition of uncovering his awrah while standing) i.e. for relieving himself until he comes close to the ground, being cautious about uncovering the awrah without necessity due to the saying of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him): 'When the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) wanted to relieve himself, he would not lift his garment until he came close to the ground.' Narrated by Tirmidhi with a good chain. Al-Abyari said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: Its place is when he does not fear soiling, and the lifting is to the extent of need. Al-Tibi said: It is the same in the desert and buildings because uncovering the awrah is not permitted except for need, i.e. necessity, and there is no necessity before getting close to the ground. Non-permissibility is one of two opinions in seclusion according to us. And the author's words include uncovering after finishing; it is disliked either prohibitively or permittedly according to the difference of opinion regarding uncovering the awrah in seclusion. And it is recommended to wash his hand after finishing even if the place appears pure, for thorough cleansing.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of not uncovering one's private parts (awrah) until one is close to the ground when intending to relieve oneself. The proof is the hadith of Anas: the Prophet (PBUH) did not lift his garment until he was near the ground. The scholars explain that this is to avoid unnecessary exposure. There is a difference of opinion: some say it is haram to uncover without necessity, others say it is makruh tanzihi. The same applies after finishing, one should not uncover prematurely. The recommendation to wash hands after is also mentioned. In the Hanafi school, it is generally makruh tahrimi to uncover the awrah without need, even in private, based on the hadith.

Key Terms
العورة (al-'awrah): Private parts that must be covered; for men, navel to knee; for women, entire body except face and hands.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity; a situation where one must uncover for a valid reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Anas, when should one lift the garment for relieving oneself?
A) Immediately upon entering the toilet.
B) Only after squatting.
C) When close to the ground.
D) After finishing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) to uncover one's awrah before coming close to the ground when relieving oneself, following the practice of the Prophet.
