Disliked Actions During Toilet Use
List of disliked actions during toilet use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five disliked actions while on the toilet according to the Hanafi school and explain why one of them is disliked.

Core Idea
Many normal actions become disliked on the toilet due to impurity and the place's nature.

This lesson covers the specific actions that a Muslim should avoid while on the toilet. The source text enumerates these prohibitions to remind the believer that even in the most private settings, the etiquettes of Islam apply. Understanding these rulings helps maintain respect for the place and awareness of Allah's presence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Read the passage and note that most of the listed actions are prohibited or disliked. The author uses 'لا' to indicate prohibition.
2
Classify each action
For each action, determine if it is makruh (disliked) or haram. In the Hanafi school, actions like returning greetings are makruh.
3
Note the exceptions
Some actions like mentioning Allah are also prohibited, but the supplication after leaving is recommended.
4
Understand the rationale
The passage explains that prolonged sitting causes health issues. This shows that Islamic etiquette also considers physical well-being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وذكر الله فلا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد سلاماً ولا مؤذناً ولا ينظر لعورته ولا إلى الخارج منها ولا يبصق ولا يتمخط ولا يتنحن ولا يكثر الإلتفات، ولا يعبث ببدنه ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء ولا يطيل الجلوس لأنه يورث الباسور، ووجع الكبد ويخرج من الخلاء برجله اليمنى لأنها أحق بالتقدم لنعمة الإنصراف الأذى ومحل الشياطين (ثم يقول) بعد الخروج (الحمد الله الذي أذهب عني الأذى) بخروج الفضلات الممرضة بحبسها وعافاني) بإبقاء خاصية الغذاء الذي لو أمسك كله أو خرج لكان مظنة الهلاك، وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عند خروجه غفرانك وهو كناية عن الإعتراف بالقصور عن بلوغ حق شكر نعمة الإطعام وتصريف خاصية الغذاء وتسهيل خروج الأذى
His saying: (And mention of Allah, so he does not praise if he sneezes, nor responds to a sneezer, nor returns a greeting, nor responds to the call to prayer, nor looks at his awrah nor at what comes out of him, nor spits, nor blows his nose, nor clears his throat, nor turns around much, nor fidgets with his body, nor raises his eyes to the sky, nor prolongs sitting because it causes hemorrhoids and liver pain, and he leaves the toilet with his right foot because it is more deserving of precedence for the blessing of leaving the filth and the dwelling of devils. (Then he says) after leaving: (Praise be to Allah who has taken away the harm from me) by the exit of waste that would cause illness if retained, and (given me health) by preserving the property of food which if all retained or exited would be a cause of destruction. And the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said upon leaving: 'Your forgiveness' which is a metaphor for acknowledging shortcomings in achieving the right to thank for the blessing of feeding and the management of the property of food and facilitation of the exit of harm.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage enumerates various disliked and prohibited actions while on the toilet. One should not engage in any form of dhikr, respond to sneezes, greetings, or adhan, nor look at private parts or excrement, nor spit, blow nose, clear throat, look around, fidget, look up, or sit too long. The reason for avoiding prolonged sitting is that it causes hemorrhoids and liver pain. One should exit with the right foot, as the right is preferred for good actions. After leaving, one should say the prescribed supplication: 'Alhamdulillah...' and also 'Ghufranak' as taught by the Prophet. The commentary explains these supplications acknowledge Allah's blessings in removing harmful waste and preserving beneficial food. These etiquettes are part of the comprehensive adab of the toilet in Islam.

Key Terms
لا يرد سلاماً (la yaruddu salaman): He does not return a greeting while on the toilet; because he is in a state of impurity.
الباسور (al-basur): Hemorrhoids; a medical condition.
غفرانك (ghufranak): Your forgiveness; a supplication acknowledging sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, prolonged sitting on the toilet is disliked because...
A) It causes hemorrhoids and liver pain.
B) It is disrespectful to the place.
C) It leads to laziness.
D) It is a waste of time.

Key Takeaway
Muslims should avoid speaking, dhikr, and fidgeting while on the toilet; after leaving, they should exit with the right foot and say the prescribed supplications.
